§ 10.01 TITLE OF CODE.
   All ordinances of a permanent and general nature, as revised, codified,
rearranged, renumbered and consolidated into component codes, titles, chapters
and sections, shall be known and designated as the “code,” for which
designation “code of ordinances” or “codified ordinances” may be substituted.
Code title, chapter and section headings do not constitute any part of the law
as contained in the code.
§ 10.02 RULES OF INTERPRETATION.
   (A)   Generally. Unless otherwise provided herein, or by law or implication
required, the same rules of construction, definition and application shall
govern the interpretation of this code as those governing the interpretation of
state law.
   (B)   Specific rules of interpretation. The construction of all ordinances
shall be by the following rules, unless that construction is plainly repugnant
to the intent of the legislative body or of the context of the same ordinance.
      (1)   Acts by assistants. When a statute, code provisions or ordinance
requires an act to be done which, by law, an agent or deputy as well may do as
the principal, that requisition shall be satisfied by the performance of the
act by an authorized agent or deputy.
      (2)   Gender; singular and plural; tenses. Words denoting the masculine
gender shall be deemed to include the feminine and neuter genders; words in the
singular shall include the plural and words in the plural shall include the
singular; the use of a verb in the present tense shall include the future, if
applicable.
      (3)   General term. A general term following specific enumeration of
terms is not to be limited to the class enumerated unless expressly so limited.
General terms descriptive of an officer, act, proceeding or thing shall have
reference to a municipality concerned or affected.
Statutory reference:
   General terms descriptive of an officer, act, proceeding and the like, see
SDCL § 9-1-1
§ 10.03 CAPTIONS.
   Headings and captions used in this code other than the title, chapter and
section numbers are employed for reference purposes only and shall not be
deemed a part of the text of any section.
§ 10.04 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this code of ordinances, the following definitions shall
apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   COMPUTATION OF TIME. The time in which any act provided by this code or
other ordinance is to be done is computed by excluding the first day and
including the last, unless the last is a holiday and then it also is excluded.
Fractions of a day are to be disregarded in computations which include more
than one day and involve no questions of priority.
   COUNTY. Lawrence County, South Dakota.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   ELECTOR(S) or QUALIFIED ELECTOR(S). Voter(s).
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   GOVERNING BODY. The Common Council of the city.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   LOT. Includes PARCEL or TRACT OF LAND.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   MONTH. A calendar month.
   MUNICIPALITY or MUNICIPAL CORPORATION. The City of Spearfish, South Dakota.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   ORDINANCE. A permanent legislative act within the limits of its powers of
the governing body of a municipality.
(SDCL § 9-19-1)
   OWNER. As used in this code relating to local improvements, the grantee in
the last deed of conveyance of any lot or parcel of land recorded in the office
of the register of deeds of the county or counties in which the municipality is
located, or his or her heirs or successors.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   PUBLICATION. Any requirement for publication shall mean publication in the
official newspaper of the municipality concerned or affected, if any; but if
none, then, in a legal newspaper published in such municipality, if any; but if
none, then, in any legal newspaper which serves such municipality, except as
provided by SDCL § 9-13-13. Personal service either within or without the state
upon the person affected thereby by delivery of a copy of a notice required to
be published shall be equivalent to the required publication.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   RESOLUTION. Any determination, decision or direction of the governing body
of a municipality of a temporary or special character for the purpose of
initiating, effecting or carrying out its administrative duties and functions.
(SDCL § 9-19-1)
   SDCL. South Dakota Codified Laws.
   STREET. STREET includes AVENUE.
(SDCL § 9-1-1)
   YEAR. A calendar year.
§ 10.05 SEVERABILITY.
   If any provision of this code as now or later amended or its application to
any person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect
other provisions that can be given effect without the invalid provision or
application.
§ 10.06 REFERENCE TO OTHER SECTIONS.
   Whenever in one section reference is made to another section hereof, that
reference shall extend and apply to the section referred to as subsequently
amended, revised, recodified or renumbered unless the subject matter is changed
or materially altered by the amendment or revision.
§ 10.07 REFERENCES TO OFFICES.
   Reference to a public office or officer shall be deemed to apply to any
office, officer or employee of this local government exercising the powers,
duties or functions contemplated in the provision, irrespective of any transfer
of functions or change in the official title of the functionary.
§ 10.08 ERRORS AND OMISSIONS.
   If a manifest error is discovered, consisting of the misspelling of any
words; the omission of any word or words necessary to express the intention of
the provisions affected; the use of a word or words to which no meaning can be
attached; or the use of a word or words when another word or words was clearly
intended to express the intent, the spelling shall be corrected and the word or
words supplied, omitted or substituted as will conform with the manifest
intention, and the provisions shall have the same effect as though the correct
words were contained in the text as originally published. No alteration shall
be made or permitted if any question exists regarding the nature or extent of
the error.
§ 10.09 POWERS TO ENACT, AMEND OR REPEAL ORDINANCES AND RESOLUTIONS; GENERALLY.
   Every municipality may enact, make, amend, revise or repeal all such
ordinances, resolutions and regulations as may be proper and necessary to carry
into effect the powers granted thereto.
§ 10.10 ORDINANCES REPEALED.
   This code, from and after its effective date, shall contain all of the
provisions of a general nature pertaining to the subjects herein enumerated and
embraced. All prior ordinances pertaining to the subjects treated by this code
shall be deemed repealed from and after the effective date of this code.
§ 10.11 ORDINANCES UNAFFECTED.
   All ordinances of a temporary or special nature and all other ordinances
pertaining to subjects not embraced in this code shall remain in full force and
effect unless herein repealed expressly or by necessary implication.
§ 10.12 REPEAL OR MODIFICATION OF AN ORDINANCE.
   (A)   No suit, proceedings, right, fine, forfeiture or penalty instituted,
created, given, secured or accrued under any ordinance previous to its repeal
shall in any way be affected, released or discharged, but may be prosecuted,
enjoined and recovered as fully as if the ordinance had continued in force
unless it is otherwise expressly provided.
   (B)   When any ordinance repealing a former ordinance, clause or provision
shall be itself repealed, the repeal shall not be construed to revive the
former ordinance, clause or provision, unless it is expressly provided.
§ 10.13 ORDINANCES WHICH AMEND OR SUPPLEMENT CODE.
   (A)   If the legislative body shall desire to amend any existing chapter or
section of this code, the chapter or section shall be specifically repealed and
a new chapter or section, containing the desired amendment, substituted in its
place.
   (B)   Any ordinance which is proposed to add to the existing code a new
chapter or section shall indicate, with reference to the arrangement of this
code, the proper number of the chapter or section. In addition to this
indication as may appear in the text of the proposed ordinance, a caption or
title shall be shown in concise form above the ordinance.
§ 10.14 PRESERVATION OF PENALTIES, OFFENSES, RIGHTS AND LIABILITIES.
   All offenses committed under laws in force prior to the effective date of
this code shall be prosecuted and remain punishable as provided by those laws.
This code does not affect any rights or liabilities accrued, penalties incurred
or proceedings begun prior to the effective date of this code. The liabilities,
proceedings and rights are continued; punishments, penalties or forfeitures
shall be enforced and imposed as if this code had not been enacted. In
particular, any agreement granting permission to utilize highway rights-of-way,
contracts entered into or franchises granted, the acceptance, establishment or
vacation of any highway, and the election of corporate officers shall remain
valid in all respects, as if this code had not been enacted.
§ 10.99 GENERAL PENALTY.
   Whenever in this code or in any ordinance of the city an act is prohibited
or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense or a misdemeanor, or
wherever in such code or ordinance the doing of any act is required, or the
failure to do any act is declared unlawful and no specific penalty is provided
therefor, any person who shall be convicted of any such violation shall be
fined not more than $500. Each day any violation of this code or other
ordinance continues shall constitute a separate offense.
(Prior Code, § 1-14) (Ord. 899, passed 7-16-2001; Ord. 1060, passed 7-2-2007)
Statutory reference:
   Penalty for violation of ordinances, see SDCL § 9-19-3
CHAPTER 11: CITY STANDARDS
Section
   
11.01   Corporate limits
   
11.02   Seal
§ 11.01 CORPORATE LIMITS.
   The corporate limits of the city are hereby declared to be such as have
heretofore and hereafter been legally established and amended by law and
ordinances of the city as shown on the official map thereof on file in the
office of the City Finance Officer, and such map is incorporated in this code
by reference and adopted as the official map showing the boundaries and limits
of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2-1)
§ 11.02 SEAL.
   (A)   The seal of the city shall have engraved thereon the words “City of
Spearfish, South Dakota, Seal, Incorporated.” The city seal shall be and remain
in the custody of the City Finance Officer.
   (B)   The seal of the city shall be affixed by the City Finance Officer to
all ordinances passed by the Council, warrants ordered drawn for the payment of
money from the City Finance Officer, bonds and any and all other instruments to
which the seal shall be attached as required by the statute. The City Finance
Officer shall pay no warrant or order for money unless the seal shall be
affixed thereto.
(Prior Code, § 2-2)
Statutory reference:
   City seal, see SDCL § 9-1-4

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 30.01 ELECTIVE OFFICERS.
   The elective officers of the city shall consist of the Mayor who is elected
at large for a term of three years and two aldermen elected from each ward for
a term of three years. They shall be elected and qualified, and their duties
shall be as defined as provided by the state law and ordinances of this city.
(Prior Code, § 2-21) (Ord. 946, passed 1-21-2003)
Statutory reference:
   Common Council, see SDCL §§ 9-8-4 through 9-8-11
   Mayor, see SDCL §§ 9-8-1 through 9-8-4
   Term of Mayor established by ordinance, see SDCL § 9-8-1
§ 30.02 MAYOR’S DUTIES GENERALLY.
   The Mayor shall be the chief executive and administrative officer of the
city government, shall enforce the laws of the city and shall require the
faithful performances of all administrative duties.
(Prior Code, § 2-22)
Statutory reference:
   Duties of the Mayor, see SDCL § 9-8-3
§ 30.03 MAYOR TO APPOINT COMMITTEES.
   The Mayor shall appoint such committees of the Common Council as may be
necessary for the transaction of business and the administration of the affairs
of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2-23)
MEETINGS
§ 30.15 REGULAR MEETINGS.
   (A)   The Common Council shall hold regular meetings on the first and third
Monday of each and every month of the year at the hour of 5:30 p.m. Whenever
the day fixed for any regular meeting of the Council falls upon a day
designated by law as a legal or national holiday, then such meetings shall be
held on the first workday following that holiday at 5:30 p.m.
   (B)   All regular meetings of the Council shall be held in the Council
chambers of the city located in City Hall.
(Prior Code, § 2-41) (Ord. 1125, passed 10-4-2010; Ord. 1213, passed 7-6-2015)
§ 30.16 SPECIAL MEETINGS.
   The Mayor shall call special meetings of the Council whenever in his or her
opinion the public business may require it, or at the express written consent
of any two aldermen. Notice of such special meeting shall be given to each
alderman at least 24 hours before such special meeting is held either
personally or by notice by facsimile, electronic mail or telephone unless a
waiver of such notice is obtained either before or at such special meeting. The
notice required under this section shall state the date and hour of the meeting
and the purpose for which such meeting is called. No such business shall be
transacted except as stated in the notice.
(Prior Code, § 2-42) (Ord. 935, passed 10-7-2002)
§ 30.17 ADJOURNED MEETINGS.
   The Common Council may adjourn a meeting to a later date, in which event the
adjourned meeting shall be considered as a part of the first meeting.
(Prior Code, § 2-43)
§ 30.18 MEETINGS OPEN TO PUBLIC.
   The meetings of the Common Council shall be open to the public. It shall be
unlawful for any person not a member of the Council to make any disturbance or
interfere in any way with the deliberations of the Council at such meetings. No
person, not a member of the Council, shall address or deliver any remarks to
the Council at such meetings without first asking for the privilege of so
doing.
(Prior Code, § 2-44) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Open meetings, see SDCL § 9-8-8
§ 30.19 AGENDA.
   All reports, communications, ordinances, resolutions, contract documents or
other matters to be submitted to the Common Council shall be delivered to the
finance office by the Friday preceding the Council meeting. The City Finance
Officer shall arrange a list of such matters according to the order of business
and furnish each member of the Council, the Mayor and the City Attorney with a
copy of the agenda prior to the Council meeting and as far in advance of the
meeting as time for preparation will permit.
(Prior Code, § 2-45)
§ 30.20 EXECUTIVE SESSIONS.
   The Common Council, by motion, may close meetings for executive sessions for
those purposes permitted by law. Thereafter, the Council shall reconvene in
open meeting to take such actions as may be appropriate.
(Prior Code, § 2-46)
§ 30.21 PRESIDING OFFICER AND ORGANIZATION OF COUNCIL.
   The presiding officer at all meetings of the Common Council shall be the
Mayor. The City Council, at its first regular meeting after the annual
election, shall organize by electing one of its members as President and one as
Vice-President. They shall hold their respective office for the ensuing year.
The President of the Council shall in the absence of the Mayor be the presiding
officer of the Council. During any absence or temporary disability of the
Mayor, the President of the Council shall be Acting Mayor and shall possess all
the power of the Mayor. In the absence of the Mayor and the President of the
Council, the Vice-President shall perform such duties.
(Prior Code, § 2-47)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL §§ 9-8-3 and 9-8-7
§ 30.22 CALL TO ORDER.
   The Mayor or, in his or her absence, the President or Vice-President shall
take the chair precisely at the hour appointed for the meeting and shall call
the Common Council to order. In the absence of the Mayor, President and Vice-
President, the Finance Officer shall call the Council to order, whereupon a
temporary Chairperson shall be elected by the members of the Council present.
Upon the arrival of the Mayor, President or Vice-President, the temporary
Chairperson shall immediately relinquish the chair upon the conclusion of the
business immediately before the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-48)
§ 30.23 ROLL CALL.
   Before proceeding with the business of the Common Council, the Finance
Officer shall call the roll of the members, and the names of those present
shall be entered in the minutes.
(Prior Code, § 2-49)
§ 30.24 QUORUM.
   A majority of all the members elected to the Common Council shall constitute
a quorum at any regular or special meeting of the Council. In the absence of a
quorum, the presiding officer shall, at the instance of any two members
present, compel the attendance of absent members.
(Prior Code, § 2-50)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 9-8-8
§ 30.25 COMPEL ATTENDANCE.
   The Common Council may compel the presence of absent members by sending the
Chief of Police or any police officer to require their attendance. If any
member refuses to attend after being notified, he or she shall state his or her
reasons therefor to the Council at its next meeting, and if the Council,
excluding the member whose refusal to attend is under consideration,
unanimously deems such reasons insufficient in light of all circumstances, the
Council may impose such penalty which in their discretion the case warrants.
(Prior Code, § 2-51)
§ 30.26 READING OF MINUTES.
   Unless a reading of the minutes of a Council meeting is requested by a
member of the Council, such minutes may be approved without reading if the
Finance Officer has previously furnished each member with a copy of the
minutes.
(Prior Code, § 2-52)
§ 30.27 MAYOR’S VOTE.
   The Mayor shall preside at all meetings of the Council but shall be entitled
to vote only on any questions when there is a tie vote thereon. He or she shall
preserve order and decide all questions of order subject to an appeal from the
Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-53)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 9-8-3
§ 30.28 SILENCE AS AFFIRMATIVE VOTE.
   Unless a member of the Council states that he or she is not voting, his or
her silence shall be recorded as an affirmative vote.
(Prior Code, § 2-54)
§ 30.29 RULES OF ORDER.
   Robert’s Rules of Order, Newly Revised, as published by Scott, Foresman and
Company, shall govern the Council in its deliberation in cases not otherwise
provided for by ordinance, rule or regulation.
(Prior Code, § 2-55)

COUNCIL ON THE ARTS AND HUMANITIES
§ 31.001 PURPOSE.
   The artists and artistic institutions of the city contribute to and provide
cultural, educational, entertainment and recreational benefits available to and
used by the citizens of the city. The establishment of the City Area Council on
the Arts and Humanities has promoted and encouraged public programs to further
the development and public awareness of and interest in the arts which is
essential to the public welfare. Therefore, the Common Council does hereby
designate the City Area Council on the Arts and Humanities as the organization
to assist the city in promoting and encouraging public programs to further the
development and awareness of and interest in the arts and to act in an advisory
capacity to the Council in connection with the artistic and cultural
development of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2-96) (Ord. 628, passed 11-16-1987)
§ 31.002 DUTY GENERALLY; RECEIPT, DISTRIBUTION OF FUNDS.
   (A)   In furtherance of the objectives of this subchapter, the City Area
Council on the Arts and Humanities is to initiate, sponsor and conduct public
programs to further the development and awareness of and interest in the arts.
   (B)   The Common Council does hereby authorize the City Area Council on the
Arts and Humanities to receive and distribute funds on behalf of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2-97) (Ord. 628, passed 11-16-1987)
§ 31.003 ADVISORY CAPACITY.
   The City Area Council on the Arts and Humanities is to advise and assist the
city in connection with such other artistic activities as may be referred to it
by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-98) (Ord. 628, passed 11-16-1987)
BLACK HILLS AIRPORT TASK FORCE
§ 31.015 AUTHORIZATION.
   Upon the recommendation of the Council, the Mayor may, as needs arise,
appoint an Airport Task Force.
(Prior Code, § 2-99) (Ord. 1232, passed 1-19-2016; Ord. 1304, passed 11-4-2019)
§ 31.016 PURPOSE.
   The Task Force will advise and give recommendations to the Council on the
airport matter referred to the Task Force by the Council. The Task Force will
have no authority to exercise sovereign power.
(Prior Code, § 2-100) (Ord. 1232, passed 1-19-2016; Ord. 1304, passed 11-4-
2019)
§ 31.017 COMPOSITION.
   The Task Force will be composed of the number of members as the Council
directs. The members will be appointed by the Mayor and approved by the
Council. At least one member must be a Council member. Members will not receive
compensation for their service on the Task Force. The Task Force may, at its
first meeting, elect from among its members a Chairperson, Vice-Chairperson and
Secretary. If the Task Force chooses to elect officers, the officers are
responsible for scheduling and conducting the meetings as well as compiling the
recommendations of the Task Force to be presented to the Council. Subject to
the approval by the Council, the Mayor may remove any member.
(Prior Code, § 2-101) (Ord. 1232, passed 1-19-2016; Ord. 1304, passed 11-4-
2019)
§ 31.018 PROCEDURES OF THE TASK FORCE.
   The Task Force will perform the functions as assigned to it by the Council
and will continue for so long as the Council directs.
(Prior Code, § 2-102) (Ord. 1232, passed 1-19-2016; Ord. 1304, passed 11-4-
2019)
BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT
§ 31.030 BOARD CREATED OR CONTINUED.
   There is hereby created or continued the Board of Adjustment.
(Prior Code, § 2-107) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.031 COMPOSITION, MEMBERSHIP, QUALIFICATIONS AND REMOVAL.
   The members of the Board of Adjustment shall be the Mayor and the Common
Council. The Mayor shall appoint, subject to the approval of the Common
Council, a first and second alternate. If a member of the Board of Adjustment
is unable to consider an issue due to absence or conflict of interest, the
first alternate or second alternate, in turn, shall serve in the absent
member’s place. The first and second alternates shall each be appointed for a
term of three years. The alternates may serve two consecutive terms. Vacancies
shall be filled for the unexpired term of any alternates whose term becomes
vacant. Each alternate shall be a resident of the city. Members shall serve
without compensation for their duties.
(Prior Code, § 2-108) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.032 POWERS.
   The Board of Adjustment shall have jurisdiction over all matters
specifically authorized by law or ordinance and shall exercise all powers
conferred to it by law or ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 2-109) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.033 RULES.
   The Board of Adjustment shall adopt and be governed by rules and procedures
kept on file in the office of the Zoning Administrator.
(Prior Code, § 2-110) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.034 LEGAL ADVISOR.
   The City Attorney shall be the legal advisor of the Board of Adjustment.
(Prior Code, § 2-111) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
PLANNING COMMISSION
§ 31.045 COMMISSION CREATED OR CONTINUED.
   There is hereby created or continued the Planning Commission.
(Prior Code, § 2-112) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.046 COMPOSITION, MEMBERSHIP, QUALIFICATIONS AND REMOVAL.
   (A)   The members of the Planning Commission shall be appointed by the Mayor
and subject to the approval of the Common Council.
   (B)   Every decision upon which the Planning Commission is to make a
recommendation or a decision according to law or ordinance shall be decided by
majority vote of the present and voting members.
   (C)   Each member of the Planning Commission shall be a resident of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 2-113) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016; Ord. 1383, passed 10-6-
2023)
§ 31.047 POWERS.
   The Planning Commission shall have jurisdiction over all matters
specifically authorized by law or ordinance and shall exercise all powers
conferred to it by law or ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 2-114) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.048 RULES.
   The Planning Commission shall adopt and be governed by rules and procedures
kept on file in the office of the Zoning Administrator.
(Prior Code, § 2-115) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
§ 31.049 LEGAL ADVISOR.
   The City Attorney shall be the legal advisor of the Planning Commission.
(Prior Code, § 2-115.01) (Ord. 1233, passed 2-19-2016)
PARKS, RECREATION AND FORESTRY
ADVISORY BOARD
§ 31.060 BOARD CREATED OR CONTINUED.
   There is hereby created or continued the City Parks, Recreation and Forestry
Advisory Board (SPRFAB).
(Prior Code, § 2-115.21) (Ord. 1244, passed 7-5-2016)
§ 31.061 COMPOSITION, APPOINTMENT AND REMOVAL.
   The members of the SPRFAB shall be appointed and removed by the Mayor,
subject to the approval of the Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-115.22) (Ord. 1244, passed 7-5-2016; Ord. 1382, passed 10-2-
2023)
§ 31.062 POWERS.
   The SPRFAB is an advisory body and shall make recommendations to the Common
Council concerning recreation, physical fitness, sports and cultural programs,
activities, opportunities and services; the acquisition, operation,
supervision, use, maintenance and development of recreation and park areas and
facilities; and regulations for tree planting, removal and maintenance of
trees, bushes, shrubs and other woody vegetation on public and private
property.
(Prior Code, § 2-115.23) (Ord. 1244, passed 7-5-2016)
§ 31.063 BYLAWS.
   The SPRFAB shall adopt and be governed by bylaws, which shall be subject to
the approval of the Common Council and kept on file in the finance office.
(Prior Code, § 2-115.24) (Ord. 1244, passed 7-5-2016)
§ 31.064 URBAN FORESTRY BOARD.
   The SPRFAB shall act as the Urban Forestry Board and exercise any duties
delegated to such Board.
(Prior Code, § 2-115.25) (Ord. 1244, passed 7-5-2016)
FIRE DEPARTMENT
§ 31.075 COMPOSITION; POLICY.
   There is hereby continued the City Fire Department, which shall consist of a
career Fire Chief, career assistant chief and career administrative assistant;
with other emergency response and support personnel serving in volunteer
positions. Officer positions below the rank of Fire Chief shall be determined
and selected by the Fire Chief; and the Common Council from time to time, by
resolution, may hire additional personnel and may approve volunteers upon
recommendation by the Fire Chief.
(Prior Code, § 7-21) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.076 FIRE CHIEF.
   The Fire Chief shall be hired by the city in the same manner as other
department heads employed by the city. The Fire Chief shall be responsible for
all matters pertaining to the administration and operations of the City Fire
Department. The Fire Chief shall develop and implement policies and procedures
to govern administration and operation of the Department and shall be
responsible for the discipline, training, records and conduct of all Fire
Department personnel, to include career and volunteer. Under the general
direction of the Mayor and/or the City Administrator, the Fire Chief shall be
responsible for the enforcement of all laws, ordinances and regulations
pertaining to fire protection; and for the care and maintenance of all property
of the Fire Department. The Fire Chief, or his or her designated officer, shall
respond to all calls for service and emergency incidents, shall direct all
activities at said incidents and shall prepare reports that document response
activities, to the degree necessary, to meet and comply with city, state and
national reporting requirements.
(Prior Code, § 7-22) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.077 VOLUNTEER PERSONNEL.
   (A)   Application and eligibility. To be considered for service with the
Fire Department, individuals must complete a Fire Department application, and
all applicants shall be considered in a manner consistent with the city
standards for selecting volunteers. Upon approval by the Common Council, the
applicant shall be placed on the volunteer roster for liability and workers
compensation purposes.
(Prior Code, § 7-23)
   (B)   Duties generally; qualifications.
      (1)   Volunteer personnel shall perform official Department duties as
directed by the ranking command officer and in compliance with city and Fire
Department policies and procedures. All volunteer personnel shall be physically
able to perform the duties for the position in which they serve.
      (2)   Failure to maintain compliance with Department policies, procedures
and standards shall be cause for discipline or removal.
(Prior Code, § 7-24)
   (C)   Volunteer incentive and reimbursement. Volunteer personnel may receive
incentives and reimbursements as established from time to time, by resolution
of the Common Council, in accordance with the current adopted fiscal year
budget. Fire Department personnel, who are career employees, shall be
compensated under the city’s pay plan and shall not receive the compensation
detailed in this section.
(Prior Code, § 7-25)
   (D)   Volunteer recruitment. The city is responsible for recruitment of
volunteers.
(Prior Code, § 7-26)
(Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.078 EXTRATERRITORIAL FIRE PROTECTION.
   The city may provide fire protection services to other political
subdivisions, rural areas adjoining the corporate limits or other governmental
agencies by contract or written agreement. The Common Council shall determine
the extent of such coverage and shall approve any contract or agreement by
resolution.
(Prior Code, § 7-27) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.079 JOINT SERVICE.
   The Common Council may, by contract or other agreement, provide joint
services with other local, county, state or federal governmental entities or
quasi-governmental entities; during major fires or other incidents.
(Prior Code, § 7-28) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.080 DEFERRED COMPENSATION PLAN.
   (A)   Generally. There shall be a deferred compensation plan for volunteer
personnel. The contribution rates and governing policy of the deferred
compensation plan shall be established by resolution of the Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 7-29)
   (B)   Funding. The deferred compensation plan shall be funded initially by
an appropriation from the city and thereafter by appropriation as may be
budgeted and such other funds as may be available.
(Prior Code, § 7-30)
   (C)   Deferred Compensation Plan Committee; membership. The deferred
compensation plan shall be managed by a Deferred Compensation Plan Committee in
accordance with all applicable state and federal laws and regulations. The
Deferred Compensation Plan Committee shall be appointed by the Mayor and
ratified by the Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 7-31)
   (D)   Termination. Should the deferred compensation plan terminate, all
unpaid and unobligated funds shall revert to the city.
(Prior Code, § 7-32)
(Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.081 AUTHORITY AT EMERGENCY INCIDENTS.
   Within the corporate limits of the city and within response areas under
contractual authority of the city, the Fire Chief or in his or her absence, a
designee, while operating at the scene of an emergency incident, or call for
service under command of the City Fire Department, shall have the sole control
over all Fire Department personnel at said incident.
(Prior Code, § 7-33) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.082 DESTRUCTION OF BUILDINGS.
   The Fire Chief or in his or her absence a designee may, in his or her best
professional judgment and training, order the destruction of any building or
structure for the purpose of extinguishing and checking any fire and preserving
life, health, safety or property.
(Prior Code, § 7-34) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
§ 31.083 APPARATUS GENERALLY.
   All fire trucks, together with all other firefighting equipment, vehicles
and apparatus, shall be housed in buildings to be furnished by the Common
Council and shall be used only under the supervision of the City Fire
Department and under such orders and regulations as the Common Council may from
time to time prescribe.
(Prior Code, § 7-35) (Ord. 1227, passed 1-4-2016; Ord. 1290, passed 8-20-2018)
CHAPTER 32: OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES

32.01   Officers

§ 32.01 OFFICERS.
   (A)   The officers of the city shall be a City Administrator who shall be
hired by the Mayor and approved by the Common Council.
   (B)   The City Administrator’s employment is subject to the city’s personnel
policies and procedures and any employment contract.
(Prior Code, § 2-116) (Ord. 938, passed 11-4-2002; Ord. 1367, passed 6-21-2022)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 9-14-3
§ 32.02 OATH OF OFFICER.
   (A)   Each officer and such other officers as may be required shall take an
oath of office before entering upon the discharge of duties.
   (B)   The oath shall be subscribed by the person taking it and shall be
filed and preserved in the office of the Finance Officer.
(Prior Code, § 2-117) (Ord. 938, passed 11-4-2002)
Statutory reference:
   Oath, see SDCL § 9-14-6
§ 32.03 BONDS.
   Bonds of city officials, unless otherwise provided for by state law, shall
be as fixed annually at the May meeting by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-118)
Statutory reference:
   Bond, see SDCL §§ 9-14-6 and 9-14-6.1
§ 32.04 PERSONNEL POLICY AND PROCEDURES.
   (A)   All personnel policies and procedures governing conditions of
employment by the city, except as otherwise provided in this code, shall be
contained in a manual, entitled “Personnel Policies and Procedures” adopted by
the Common Council in the same manner as all other ordinances, which is on file
in the office of the Finance Officer.
   (B)   The city shall adopt a safety manual with procedures and practices
designed to keep city employees and facilities safe. The safety manual may be
amended from time to time by the Safety Committee or the City Administrator. A
copy of the current safety manual shall be kept on file in the finance office
and on the employee portal.
(Prior Code, § 2-119) (Ord. 741, passed 5-3-1993; Ord. 1175, passed 4-1-2013;
Ord. 1255, passed 11-21-2016)
§ 32.05 REMOVAL OF OFFICIALS.
   The Mayor may remove from office any officer appointed by the Mayor, if the
Mayor believes that the interests of the city demand such removal. The Mayor
shall report the reasons for removal to the Council at its next regular
meeting.
(Prior Code, § 2-120) (Ord. 938, passed 11-4-2002; Ord. 1367, passed 6-21-2022)
Statutory reference:
   Removal of appointed officers, see SDCL § 9-14-13
§ 32.06 FINANCE OFFICER’S REPORT.
   The Finance Officer shall report the financial condition of the several
funds and such other information relating thereto as may be in his or her
possession to the Common Council every month. The monthly report shall be made
to the Council on a regular meeting night.
(Prior Code, § 2-121)
§ 32.07 RETIREMENT SYSTEM.
   The city shall become a participating municipality in the South Dakota
Retirement System, as provided by law, for the purpose of including all
employees in its employ under the retirement system. The effective date of the
city’s participation in the retirement system shall be January 1, 1966.
(Prior Code, § 2-122)
Statutory reference:
   Retirement systems and pensions, see SDCL §§ 9-16-1 et seq.
   South Dakota Retirement System, see SDCL Ch. 3-12C
§ 32.08 CITY ADMINISTRATOR APPOINTMENT; QUALIFICATIONS; COMPENSATION, REMOVAL.
   The Common Council may appoint a City Administrator for an indefinite term
and fix the Administrator’s compensation. The City Administrator shall be
appointed solely on the basis of executive and administrative qualifications.
The City Administrator need not be a resident of the city or state at the time
of appointment but may reside outside the city while in office in conjunction
with his or her employment agreement. The City Administrator, as an officer of
the city, may be removed by the Mayor.
(Prior Code, § 2-124) (Ord. 1280, passed 5-7-2018; Ord. 1319, passed 7-6-2020)
§ 32.09 POWERS AND DUTIES OF THE CITY ADMINISTRATOR.
   (A)   Notwithstanding the provisions of §
30.02, the City Administrator shall be the chief administrative officer of the
city, responsible to the Common Council and Mayor for the administration of all
city affairs placed in the Administrator’s charge by this code or other
ordinances and resolutions of the city.
   (B)   The City Administrator shall:
      (1)   See that all provisions of this code and all acts of the Common
Council subject to enforcement by the City Administrator or employees subject
to the Administrator’s direction and supervision, are faithfully executed;
      (2)   Oversee and direct the administration of all departments, offices
and agencies of the city, except as otherwise provided by this code or by state
law;
      (3)   Make recommendations to the Common Council concerning the affairs
of the city;
      (4)   Prepare and submit to the Common Council an annual budget not later
than September 1 of each year;
      (5)   Ensure all terms and conditions in any contract or franchise to
which the city is a party are faithfully kept and performed;
      (6)   Direct the hiring, reassignment and promotion of all city
employees;
      (7)   When necessary, suspend or remove any city employee except as
otherwise provided by law, this code or adopted personnel policies;
      (8)   Consolidate or combine offices, positions, departments or units
under his or her jurisdiction;
      (9)   Serve as the liaison between city staff, the Mayor and the Common
Council;
      (10)   Attend all meetings of the Common Council, except as excused by
the Mayor;
      (11)   Keep the Common Council fully advised as to the future needs of
the city;
      (12)   Provide for staff support services for the Mayor and Council
members;
      (13)   Submit updates and reports to the Common Council as requested;
      (14)   Delegate authority as deemed appropriate; and
      (15)   Perform such other duties as are required by the position
description specified in this code, by resolution or as may be required from
time to time by the Mayor or Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-125) (Ord. 1280, passed 5-7-2018; Ord. 1319, passed 7-6-2020;
Ord. 1366, passed 6-21-2022)
§ 32.10 ACTING CITY ADMINISTRATOR; REVOCATION AND ALTERNATIVE APPOINTMENT.
   By letter filed with the Finance Officer, the City Administrator shall
designate a city officer or employee to exercise the powers and perform the
duties of City Administrator during the Administrator’s temporary absence or
disability. The Common Council may revoke such designation at any time and
appoint another officer of the city to serve until the City Administrator
returns.
(Prior Code, § 2-126) (Ord. 1280, passed 5-7-2018)
§ 32.11 AUTHORITY TO APPROVE EXPENDITURES AND ENTER INTO CITY CONTRACTS.
   The Mayor or City Administrator have the authority to sign and approve any
expenditures, contracts or agreements on behalf of the city that are less than
the bid limits established under state law for public improvement contracts.
Such expenditures, contracts or agreements that exceed $25,000 shall be
countersigned by either the Finance Officer or the City Attorney. No claim may
be paid until approved by the Common Council, except as may be otherwise
provided by ordinance or resolution.
(Prior Code, § 2-127) (Ord. 1319, passed 7-6-2020)
CHAPTER 33: ELECTIONS
Section

§ 33.01 DIVISION INTO WARDS.
   The city is hereby divided into three wards.
(Prior Code, § 2-141) (Ord. 730, passed 7-20-1992)
Statutory reference:
   Determination of wards, see SDCL § 9-2-7
§ 33.02 WARD ONE.
   All that portion of the city lying west of Spearfish Creek starting from the
municipal boundary on Winterville Road to the intersection of Hillsview Road
and Spearfish Creek, then all portions lying north of Hillsview Road and west
of North Avenue/Highway 85 and south of Highway 14, shall constitute the first
ward.
(Prior Code, § 2-142) (Ord. 730, passed 7-20-1992; Ord. 1114, passed 12-21-
2009; Ord. 1149, passed 12-5-2011)
§ 33.03 WARD TWO.
   All that portion of the city not located in the first ward, lying east of
Spearfish Creek and south of Interstate 90 between Maitland Road to Sandstone
Hills Drive, then all portions lying south of Colorado Boulevard at Sandstone
Hills Drive to the intersection of Dahl Road and Colorado Boulevard, then all
portions lying south of Dahl Road to the 10th Street intersection, then all
portions lying south and west of the 10th Street and Dahl Road intersection to
the intersection of 10th Street and Dakota Street, then all portions lying
south and west of the 10th Street and Dakota Street intersection to the
intersection of 7th Street and Dakota Street, then all portions lying south and
west of the 7th Street and Dakota Street intersection, then from the 7th Street
and Dakota Street intersection to the 7th Street and Michigan Street
intersection, all portions lying south of Michigan Street and west of 7th
Street to Spearfish Creek, then to the intersection of Michigan Street and Main
Street, all portions lying south and west of the intersections of Michigan
Street and Main Street, then at the intersection of Michigan Street and Main
Street, all portions lying west of North Avenue and south of Hillsview Road,
shall constitute the second ward. Where a parcel of land along Spearfish Creek
is split between Ward One and Ward Two, the location of the residence shall
determine the ward pertaining to the voter.
(Prior Code, § 2-143) (Ord. 324, passed 9-17-1973; Ord. 730, passed 7-20-1992;
Ord. 943, passed 12-16-2002; Ord. 1114, passed 12-21-2009; Ord. 1149, passed
12-5-2011; Ord. 1360, passed 1-3-2022)
§ 33.04 WARD THREE.
   All that portion of the city, not located in the first or second wards,
lying east of Spearfish Creek, shall constitute the third ward.
(Prior Code, § 2-144) (Ord. 730, passed 7-20-1992; Ord. 1114, passed 12-21-
2009; Ord. 1149, passed 12-5-2011)
§ 33.05 RUNOFF ELECTION.
   (A)   In the case of a tie vote for Mayor or a City Council position in any
city municipal election, wherein those receiving tie votes are the candidates
receiving the highest number of votes cast regardless whether that election is
conducted by the city or held as a joint election with the county, the tie vote
will be resolved by a runoff election to be held two weeks following the
regular city election, or at the conclusion of any recount, whichever occurs
later. Only the persons who received the tie votes in the regular election will
be on the ballot of the runoff election. The person receiving the highest
number of votes in the runoff election will be considered elected.
   (B)   This section is adopted pursuant to the provisions of SDCL § 9-13-25,
and any runoff election shall be held pursuant to the provisions of SDCL § 9-
13-27.1.
(Prior Code, § 2-145) (Ord. 1094, passed 6-15-2009)
§ 33.06 ELECTION TO FILL VACANCY.
   (A)   Any vacancy in the governing body of the city or the office of Mayor
shall be filled by a special election called for that purpose as provided by
SDCL §§ 9-13-14 and 9-13-14.2. No special election may be held less than six
months before the annual municipal election.
   (B)   If there is a vacancy from any cause in the office of the Mayor less
than six months before the annual municipal election, the vacancy shall be
filled by appointment by a majority vote of the members-elect of the Common
Council, as soon as practicable after the vacancy occurs, to serve until the
office is filled by election for the unexpired term at the next annual
municipal election.
   (C)   If there is a vacancy from any cause on the Common Council less than
six months before the annual municipal election, the vacancy shall be filled by
appointment of a majority vote of the members-elect of the Common Council, as
soon as practicable after the vacancy occurs, to serve until the office is
filled by election for the unexpired term at the next annual municipal
election. The appointment must be a person from the same ward in which the
vacancy exists.
   (D)   Any special election shall be held according to the procedures
required by SDCL §§ 9-13-14 and 9-13-14.2.
(Prior Code, § 2-146) (Ord. 1095, passed 6-15-2009)
§ 33.07 ELECTION DATE.
   The regular municipal election of the city is hereby scheduled on the first
Tuesday after the first Monday in April. The Common Council may elect to hold a
municipal election in conjunction with a primary election or school district
election. Elections shall be conducted in accordance with SDCL Ch. 9-13.
(Prior Code, § 2-147) (Ord. 1115, passed 1-4-2010; Ord. 1169, passed 1-22-2013;
Ord. 1234, passed 2-16-2016)

RURAL SERVICE DISTRICTS
§ 34.01 GROSS RECEIPTS TAX.
   SDCL Ch. 9-21A provides that lands that are rural in character, are used or
usable for agriculture and are not developed for commercial, industrial or
residential purposes, are not benefited to the same degree as other lands by
municipal services financed by general taxation. Such land may be placed in a
Rural Service District and will not be subject to municipal property tax until
removed.
(Prior Code, § 16-1) (Ord. 936, passed 10-21-2002)
§ 34.02 AUTHORITY.
   This subchapter is adopted pursuant to the authority granted by SDCL Ch. 9-
21A. Land placed in a Rural Service District shall benefit from such
designation until removed under the criteria set forth in §
34.04.
(Prior Code, § 16-2) (Ord. 936, passed 10-21-2002)
§ 34.03 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   COMMERCIAL. As ordinarily defined.
   INDUSTRIAL. As ordinarily defined.
   RESIDENTIAL DEVELOPMENT. A major subdivision of more than three lots, having
a density equal to or greater than one lot per two acres.
(Prior Code, § 16-3) (Ord. 936, passed 10-21-2002)
§ 34.04 CRITERIA FOR REMOVAL FROM DISTRICT.
   (A)   If any of the following criteria are met, the Common Council, by
order, shall remove the property, in whole or in affected part, from the
District:
      (1)   When a parcel in a Rural Service District is platted and developed
or used for the purpose of commercial, industrial or residential development;
      (2)   When a planned unit development final plan is approved for all or
part of the District, the portion approved for such development shall be
removed from the District upon the issuance of a building permit;
      (3)   When municipal water and/or sewer service is extended to the
District, that platted portion served by such service shall be removed from the
District;
      (4)   When access to or within the District is from a street dedicated to
and accepted by the city, that platted portion directly served by such street
shall be removed from the District; and
      (5)   After removing the property from the District, the remaining
portion, if comprised of 20 acres or more, may remain in the District.
   (B)   A copy of the Council’s order shall be given to the County Director of
Equalization and the property owner.
(Prior Code, § 16-4) (Ord. 936, passed 10-21-2002)
SALES, SERVICE AND USE TAX
§ 34.15 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to provide additional needed revenue for
the city by imposing a municipal retail sales and use tax pursuant to the
powers granted to the municipality by the state by SDCL Ch. 10-52 entitled
Uniform Municipal Non-Ad Valorem Tax Law and acts amendatory thereto.
(Prior Code, § 16-51) (Ord. 961, passed 7-21-2003)
§ 34.16 TAX LEVIED.
   From and after the January 1, 2004, there is hereby imposed a municipal
retail occupational sales and service tax upon the privilege of engaging in
business a tax measured by 2% on the gross receipts of all persons engaged in
the business within the jurisdiction of the city who are subject to the State
Retail Occupational Sales and Service Tax, SDCL Ch. 10-45 and acts amendatory
thereto.
(Prior Code, § 16-52) (Ord. 961, passed 7-21-2003)
§ 34.17 COLLECTION.
   The tax levied under this subchapter is pursuant to authorization granted by
SDCL Ch. 10-52, and acts amendatory thereto, and shall be collected by the
State Department of Revenue in accordance with the same rules and regulations
applicable to the state sales tax and under such additional rules and
regulations as the State Secretary of Revenue and Regulation shall lawfully
prescribe.
(Prior Code, § 16-53) (Ord. 961, passed 7-21-2003)
§ 34.18 USE TAX.
   In addition, there is hereby imposed an excise tax on the privilege of use,
storage and consumption within the jurisdiction of the city of tangible
personal property or services purchased from and after January 1, 2004, at the
same rate as the municipal sales and service tax upon all transactions or use,
storage and consumption which are subject to the State Use Tax Act, SDCL Ch.
10-46 and acts amendatory thereto.
(Prior Code, § 16-54) (Ord. 961, passed 7-21-2003)
Statutory reference:
   Use tax, see SDCL Ch. 10-46
§ 34.19 INTERPRETATION.
   It is declared to be the intention of this subchapter and the taxes levied
hereunder that the same shall be interpreted and construed in the same manner
as all sections of the State Retail Occupational Sales and Service Act, SDCL
Ch. 10-45 and acts amendatory thereto and the State Use Tax, SDCL Ch. 10-46,
and acts amendatory thereto, and that this shall be considered a similar tax
except for the rate thereof to that tax.
(Prior Code, § 16-55) (Ord. 961, passed 7-21-2003)
GROSS RECEIPTS TAX
§ 34.30 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to provide additional needed revenue for
the city by imposing a municipal non-ad valorem tax on lodgings, alcoholic
beverages and prepared food and admissions, all as described below, pursuant to
the powers granted to the municipality by the state by SDCL Ch. 10-52A and
specifically SDCL § 10-52A-2, the Uniform Municipal Non-Ad Valorem Tax Law and
acts amendatory thereto.
(Prior Code, § 16-76) (Ord. 634, passed 3-21-1988; Ord. 929, passed 8-19-2002)
§ 34.31 USE OF RECEIPTS.
   All monies received and collected on behalf of the city pursuant to this
subchapter shall be used for the purpose of land acquisition, architectural
fees, construction costs, payments for civic center, auditorium or athletic
facility buildings, including the maintenance, staffing and operation of such
facilities, and the promotion and advertising of the city, its facilities,
attractions and activities.
(Prior Code, § 16-77) (Ord. 634, passed 3-21-1988)
§ 34.32 RENTAL ACCOMMODATIONS, ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES SALES AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   Notwithstanding the rate of tax established in §
34.16, from and after January 1, 2003, there is hereby imposed a municipal
gross receipts tax of 1% upon the gross receipts of all leases or rentals of
hotel, motel, campsites or other lodging accommodations within the municipality
for periods of less than 28 consecutive days; the sales of alcoholic beverages
as defined at SDCL § 35-1-1; establishments where the public is invited to eat,
dine or purchase and carry out prepared food for immediate consumption or
ticket sales or admissions to places of amusement, athletic and cultural events
or any combination thereof.
   (B)   The tax applies to the gross receipts of all persons engaged in
business within the jurisdiction of the city, who are subject to the state’s
retail occupational sales and service tax, SDCL Ch. 10-45, and acts amendatory
thereto.
(Prior Code, § 16-78) (Ord. 634, passed 3-21-1988; Ord. 721, passed 4-6-1992;
Ord. 929, passed 8-19-2002)
§ 34.33 USE OF REVENUE.
   All revenue received and collected by the tax levied on behalf of the city
shall be used as stated in SDCL § 10-52A-2 for the purpose of land acquisition,
architectural fees, construction costs, payments for civic center, auditorium
or athletic facility buildings, including the maintenance, staffing and
operations of such facilities and the promotion and advertising of the city,
its facilities, attractions and activities.
(Prior Code, § 16-80) (Ord. 634, passed 3-21-1988; Ord. 721, passed 4-6-1992;
Ord. 929, passed 8-19-2002)
§ 34.34 COLLECTION, DISTRIBUTION, INTERPRETATION AND VIOLATIONS.
   (A)   Such tax is levied pursuant to authorization granted by SDCL Ch. 10-
52A, and acts amendatory thereto, and shall be collected by the State
Department of Revenue in accordance with the same rules and regulations
applicable to the state sales tax and under such additional rules and
regulations as the State Secretary of Revenue shall lawfully prescribe.
   (B)   It is declared to be the intention of this subchapter and the taxes
levied hereunder that the same shall be interpreted and construed in the same
manner as all sections of the State Retail Occupational Sales and Service Act,
SDCL Ch. 10-45 and acts amendatory thereto, and that this shall be considered a
similar tax except for the rate thereof to that tax.
(Prior Code, § 16-81) (Ord. 634, passed 3-21-1988; Ord. 721, passed 4-6-1992;
Ord. 929, passed 8-19-2002)
§ 34.35 IMPLEMENTATION DATE.
   Notwithstanding SDCL § 9-19-13, any new ordinance or amendment to an
ordinance enacted under the authority of this chapter and any tax rate affected
thereby, can only be effective on January 1 or July 1 of a calendar year. The
ordinance or amendment shall be effective on the earlier of January 1 or July 1
following at least 90 days’ notification by the city to the Secretary of
Revenue that the ordinance or amendment has been enacted.
(Prior Code, § 16-82) (Ord. 634, passed 3-21-1988; Ord. 721, passed 4-6-1992;
Ord. 929, passed 8-19-2002)
§ 34.36 COMPLIANCE WITH STATE LAW.
   This subchapter continues a tax which was in effect on July 1, 2002 and is
continued under the provisions of SDCL Ch. 10-52A and specifically SDCL § 10-
52A-10, the Common Council having reviewed the existing tax ordinance to
determine compliance with the provision of SDCL Ch. 10-52A and this subchapter
is adopted to comply with the provisions of SDCL Ch. 10-52A and to continue the
tax under SDCL Ch. 10-52A.
(Prior Code, § 16-84) (Ord. 929, passed 8-19-2002)
§ 34.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   Any person failing or refusing to make reports or payments prescribed
by §§
34.15 through
34.19 and the rules and regulations relating to the ascertainment and
collection of the tax herein levied shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be fined not more than $200. In addition, all such collection
remedies authorized by SDCL Ch. 10-45, and acts amendatory thereto, and SDCL
Ch. 10-46, and acts amendatory thereto, are hereby authorized for the
collection of these excise taxes by the Department of Revenue and Regulation.
(Prior Code, § 16-56)
   (C)   Any person failing or refusing to make reports or payments prescribed
by §§
34.30 through
34.36 and the rules and regulations relating to the ascertainment and
collection of the tax herein levied shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be fined not more than $200. In addition, all such collection
remedies authorized by SDCL Ch. 10-45, and acts amendatory thereto, are hereby
authorized for the collection of these excise taxes by the Department of
Revenue.
(Prior Code, § 16-81)
(Ord. 961, passed 7-21-2003)

FINANCE AND REVENUE
§ 35.01 BAD CHECKS GIVEN TO CITY OR ITS AGENTS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to make and deliver for draw and
deliver or utter or give to the city, or to any officer, employee, agent,
agency, board, bureau or commission thereof, in payment of any license, fee,
fine, penalty, assessment, tax, debt, obligation or other exaction, payment or
amount of money which the city or such officer, employee, agent, agency, board,
bureau or commission is lawfully authorized to receive or collect, any check or
draft upon any bank or banking association with knowledge that the maker or
drawer thereof does not have an account in or with such bank or banking
association subject to such check or draft.
   (B)   The fact that payment of such check or draft, when presented in the
usual course of business, shall be refused by such bank or banking association
for lack of sufficient funds to the credit of the drawer or maker with which to
pay the same, or because such drawer or maker has no account subject to such
check or draft, shall be prima facie evidence that the same was made and
delivered or drawn and delivered or uttered or given with the knowledge
hereinabove mentioned. The bad check fee to be set by resolution may be
assessed against returned checks as allowed by state law.
(Prior Code, § 2-161) (Ord. 801, passed 5-20-1996; Ord. 1102, passed 9-8-2009)
Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 35.02 ECONOMIC REVOLVING FUND.
   (A)   Established. There is established in the City Treasury a special
revenue fund to be known as the city’s Economic Revolving Fund for the purpose
of making loans for the promotion of the city.
(Prior Code, § 2-176)
   (B)   Designation of surplus revenue. The Common Council hereby determines
that there exists a surplus of sales tax revenues of at least $150,000 into the
city’s Economic Revolving Fund.
(Prior Code, § 2-177)
   (C)   Use of funds. Funds used from the city’s Economic Revolving Fund shall
be available for loans according to the criteria hereafter established by the
Common Council by resolution for the qualification, application, payment and
repayment of funds. Any repayment of loans made and any interest thereon shall
be receipted into the city’s Economic Revolving Fund, and all money in the fund
is hereby appropriated for the purposes of making loans as provided in this
section.
(Prior Code, § 2-178)
(Ord. 717, passed 1-6-1992)
§ 35.03 SERF COMMITTEE.
   (A)   Established. There is established a standing committee to be known as
the City Economic Revolving Fund (SERF) Committee for the purpose of:
      (1)   Providing technical assistance in the completion of application
documents to applicants for a SERF loan;
      (2)   Providing consultation and recommendations to the Common Council
regarding individual SERF loan applications and requests for loan servicing for
use by the Common Council in the review, evaluation and decision-making
thereon; and
      (3)   Monitoring outstanding SERF loans.
(Prior Code, § 2-179)
   (B)   Appointment of members; meetings.
      (1)   Appointment of members. Appointment of members of the SERF
Committee and establishment of the terms of service of members of the SERF
Committee shall be made by the Mayor and ratified by the Common Council. The
Committee shall consist of five members, as follows:
         (a)   The Mayor or a designee of the Mayor;
         (b)   One representative from the Common Council;
         (c)   Two representatives from the City Economic Development
Corporation; and
         (d)   One representative who is a financial or accounting
professional.
      (2)   Meetings. The SERF Committee shall meet on an as needed basis.
Following each meeting a written record of said meeting shall be prepared and
forwarded to the Common Council for review and comment.
(Prior Code, § 2-180)
   (C)   Transfers authorized. Notwithstanding any provision of division (B)
above to the contrary, the Council, by an affirmative vote of at least four
members, may authorize the transfer of funds, principal and interest, to the
West River Foundation for Economic and Community Development, Inc. to be used
as matching grant funds by the foundation in its promotion of the city pursuant
to foundation guidelines.
(Prior Code, § 2-181)
(Ord. 718, passed 2-18-1992; Ord. 885, passed 7-17-2000)
§ 35.04 LOANS TO PRIVATE PROPERTY OWNERS.
   (A)   Purpose and authority. Occasionally, an owner of private property may
be required to unexpectedly remove, repair or replace private infrastructure or
appurtenances to private property, such as a private water service line, or to
remove a large tree rendered unsafe by storm or disease. Often, such a large
and unexpected expense can create a financial hardship on a private property
owner. To reduce the effects of that hardship while still protecting public
health and safety, the city has created a short-term loan program to aid
private property owners with completing certain projects. The Finance Officer
is authorized to disburse loans to private property owners within the corporate
limits of the city in accordance with this section for the purposes of:
      (1)   Repairing or replacing a curb stop;
      (2)   Repairing or replacing a private water service line;
      (3)   Repairing or replacing a private sewer service line;
      (4)   Replacing or removing trees located within or affecting the public
right-of-way; and
      (5)   Other corrective action the city may require of an owner of private
property for the purposes of maintaining public health and safety.
(Prior Code, § 2-150)
   (B)   Amounts. No loans shall be made for less than $500. Loans shall only
exceed $3,500 with the prior approval of the Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 2-151)
   (C)   Terms.
      (1)   The Finance Officer shall develop and maintain a policy, consistent
with the provisions of this section, which sets forth:
         (a)   The payback period in months;
         (b)   The interest rate of loans;
         (c)   A loan origination fee;
         (d)   The payment due date;
         (e)   The method of payment; and
         (f)   Any other terms the Finance Officer determines are reasonable
and necessary.
      (2)   The Finance Officer may establish categories of loans based on the
amount of the loan and the terms of the loan (such as the payback period in
months) may vary between categories. However, the terms of all loans within a
single category shall be uniform regardless of the borrower.
(Prior Code, § 2-152)
   (D)   Security. Loan amounts less than $1,250 shall be unsecured. Loan
amounts in excess of $1,250 shall be secured by a mortgage on the real property
where the work is performed, which mortgage shall be recorded in the office of
the County Register of Deeds. When the loan is paid in full, a satisfaction of
mortgage shall be recorded in the office of the County Register of Deeds. The
city shall prepare and record any such documents and will pay the costs of
recording.
(Prior Code, § 2-153)
   (E)   Record and delegation of authority. Loans issued shall be documented
by a loan agreement signed by the borrower and the Finance Officer. The Finance
Officer is hereby authorized to execute loan agreements that comply with the
provisions of this section on behalf of and in the name of the city. The
Finance Officer is hereby authorized to execute mortgages and satisfactions of
mortgage pursuant to the provisions of this section.
(Prior Code, § 2-254)
(Ord. 1243, passed 5-2-2016)
ART IN PUBLIC PLACES
§ 35.15 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this subchapter is to provide a means to fund the acquisition
of artwork by the city, which shall become the city’s collection; to provide a
means to select artwork for the collection; to provide for the display of the
collection; and to provide for the maintenance and repair of the artwork in the
collection.
(Prior Code, § 14-301) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.16 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ARTWORK.
      (1)   Includes, but is not limited to, a sculpture, monument, mural,
fresco, relief, painting, fountain, banner, mosaic, ceramic, weaving, carving
and stained glass. ARTWORK would normally not include landscaping, paving,
architectural ornamentation or signs; and   
      (2)   Has been, or is intended to be, displayed for more than two weeks:
         (a)   In an open city-owned facility or property;
         (b)   On the exterior of any city-owned facility;
         (c)   Inside any city-owned facility in areas designated as public
areas;
         (d)   On any non-city property if the work is owned by the city,
installed in whole or in part with city funds; or
         (e)   On any non-city property if the owner has applied for its
placement on private property pursuant to §§
35.25 and
35.26.
   CITY. The City of Spearfish.
   COMMERCIAL DEVELOPMENT. A discrete construction project other than an
individual residential unit, a residential development or a public facility.
   COMMITTEE. The Art in Public Places Committee created and codified in §
35.18.
   CONSTRUCTION PROJECT. The construction, rehabilitation, renovation,
remodeling, equipping or improvement of any building, street, park, utility
line or other improvement, either private or for or by the city commenced after
September 1, 2005, including all associated landscaping, parking and the like,
but excluding any improvements excepted by the City Council after a public
hearing thereon.
   INDIVIDUAL RESIDENTIAL UNIT. A discrete construction project resulting in
not more than one single-family dwelling.
   PUBLIC FACILITY. A discrete construction project designed for use by the
general public.
   RESIDENTIAL DEVELOPMENT. A discrete construction project other than an
individual residential unit designed to be used primarily for human habitation,
including two or more single-family dwellings being built concurrently in the
same tract by the same owner or contractor.
(Prior Code, § 14-302) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.17 APPLICABILITY.
   All entities purchasing building permits from the city shall be subject to
the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-303) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.18 ART IN PUBLIC PLACES COMMITTEE.
   There is established an Art in Public Places Committee. It shall consist of
seven members appointed by the City Council who shall serve without
compensation. The members shall serve for periods of three years each, except
that the initial terms of two of such members shall expire on December 31,
2007, the initial terms of two such members shall expire on December 31, 2008,
and the initial terms of three such members shall expire on December 31, 2009.
All members shall be eligible for reappointment. The members shall be citizens
who are actively interested in the visual arts and civic improvement. The
function of such Committee shall be to perform the duties set forth in this
subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-304) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.19 ART IN PUBLIC PLACES FUND.
   There is established a fund known as the Art in Public Places Fund which
shall be credited with funds obtained as art in public places allocations,
secured through grants, as donations or as otherwise obtained or determined by
the City Council. This Fund shall be maintained by the City Finance Officer and
shall be used for the acquisition, installation, improvement and maintenance of
artwork to be displayed in the city, the administration of the art in public
places program and for community public art education programs, not to exceed
5% of the annual budget.
(Prior Code, § 14-305) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.20 REQUIREMENTS OF ENTITIES SUBJECT TO THIS SUBCHAPTER.
   (A)   Before the city issues a valid building permit, pursuant to §
150.018, to any entity subject to this subchapter, the entity shall fulfill one
of the following:
      (1)   An application for placement of artwork on private property has
been submitted to the Committee and approved by the City Council pursuant to §§
35.25 and
35.27;
      (2)   An application for acceptance of artwork to be donated to the city
has been submitted to the Committee and approved by the City Council pursuant
to §§
35.27 and
35.28; or
      (3)   The art in public places allocation has been paid.
   (B)   If an entity does not fulfill division (A) above prior to the
completion of the construction project, the city may assess the art in public
places allocation, pursuant to §
35.21, and this assessment therefor shall become a lien against the real
property.
(Prior Code, § 14-306) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.21 ART IN PUBLIC PLACES ALLOCATION.
   The art in public places allocation shall be 5% of the building permit cost
which is set aside for the city’s art in public places program pursuant to §
35.20(A)(3) and shall be as follows.
   (A)   The total building valuation upon which the permit cost is set shall
be computed using the latest building valuation data as set forth by the
International Building Code unless, in the opinion of the Building Official, a
different valuation should be used.
   (B)   If any project is partially funded from any source which precludes art
as an object of expenditure of funds, then this section shall apply only to the
amount of funds not so restricted.
(Prior Code, § 14-307) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.22 ADMINISTRATION.
   The Committee shall administer the provisions of this subchapter relating to
acquisition and display of artwork. The Committee shall submit to the City
Council, not later than March of each year, a report of its activities for the
prior year. The Committee shall also prepare and submit to the City Council, no
later than March of each year, an annual plan for the art in public places
program.
(Prior Code, § 14-308) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.23 GUIDELINES.
   The Committee shall adopt guidelines:
   (A)   To identify suitable artwork for city buildings;
   (B)   To facilitate the preservation of artwork;
   (C)   To prescribe a method or methods for competitive selection of artwork
for display;
   (D)   To prescribe procedures for the selection, acquisition and display of
artwork;
   (E)   To prescribe procedures for the maintenance of artwork; and
   (F)   To set forth any other matter appropriate to the administration of
this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-309) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.24 SELECTION AND DISPLAY STANDARDS.
   In performing its duties with respect to artwork, the Committee shall give
special attention to the following matters:
   (A)   Conceptual compatibility of the design with the immediate environment
of the site;
   (B)   Appropriateness of the design to the function of the site;
   (C)   Compatibility of the design and location with a unified design
character or historical character of the site;
   (D)   Creation of an internal sense of order and desirable environment for
the general community by the design and location of the artwork;
   (E)   Accessibility to the viewing and appreciation by the public;
   (F)   Preservation and integration of natural features for the project;
   (G)   Appropriateness of the materials, textures, colors and design to the
expression of the design concept; and
   (H)   Representation of a broad variety of tastes within the community and
the provision of a balanced inventory of artwork to ensure a variety of style,
design and media throughout the community.
(Prior Code, § 14-310) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.25 APPLICATION PROCEDURE FOR PLACEMENT OF ARTWORK ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   An application for placement of artwork on private property shall be
submitted to the Committee and shall include:
   (A)   Preliminary sketches, photographs or other documentation of sufficient
nature to indicate the nature of the proposed artwork;
   (B)   An appraisal or other evidence of value of the proposed artwork,
including acquisition and installation costs;
   (C)   Preliminary plans containing such detailed information as may be
required by the Committee to adequately evaluate the location of the artwork in
relation to the proposed development, and its compatibility with the proposed
development, including compatibility with the character of adjacent conforming
development parcels and existing neighborhood if necessary to evaluate the
proposal; and
   (D)   A narrative statement to be submitted to the Committee to demonstrate
that the artwork will be displayed in an area open and freely available to the
general public or otherwise provide public accessibility in an equivalent
manner based on the characteristics of the artwork or its placement on the
site.
(Prior Code, § 14-311) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.26 REVIEW OF APPLICATION FOR PLACEMENT OF ARTWORK ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   (A)   Completed applications shall be submitted to the Committee for review
and approval of the artwork.
   (B)   The Committee’s recommendation as to the approval or disapproval of
the application shall be forwarded to the City Council which shall have the
sole authority to accept or reject or conditionally accept the application.
Unapproved applications may be resubmitted to the Committee.
(Prior Code, § 14-312) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.27 APPLICATION PROCEDURE FOR ACCEPTANCE OF ARTWORK DONATED TO THE CITY.
   An application for acceptance of artwork to be donated to the city shall be
submitted to the Committee and shall include:
   (A)   Preliminary sketches, photographs, models or other documentation of
sufficient descriptive clarity to indicate the nature of the proposed artwork;
   (B)   An appraisal or other evidence of the value of the proposed artwork,
including acquisition and installation costs; and
   (C)   Other information as may be required by the Committee to adequately
evaluate the proposed donation of artwork.
(Prior Code, § 14-313) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.28 REVIEW OF APPLICATION FOR ACCEPTANCE OF ARTWORK DONATED TO THE CITY.
   (A)   Completed applications shall be submitted to the Committee for review
and approval of the donation.
   (B)   The Committee’s recommendation as to the approval or disapproval of
the donation shall be forwarded to the City Council which shall have the sole
authority to accept or reject or conditionally accept the donation. Unapproved
applications may be resubmitted to the Committee.
(Prior Code, § 14-314) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.29 ARTWORK PURCHASED WITH PUBLIC FUNDS.
   (A)   The Committee may recommend to the City Council the purchase of
artwork with funds from the Art in Public Places Fund, with city funds or with
grants procured by the city.
   (B)   A recommendation shall include the type of artwork considered, an
analysis of the constraints applicable to placement of the artwork and the
costs of acquisition and installation of the artwork.
(Prior Code, § 14-315) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.30 INSTALLATION OF ARTWORK FINANCED WITH CITY FUNDS OF PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   (A)   The Committee may install artwork financed or installed either wholly
or in part with funds from the Art in Public Places Fund, with city funds or
with grants procured by the city, on privately owned property, but only
pursuant to a written agreement between the Committee, acting on behalf of the
city, and the owner specifying the proprietary interests in the artwork and
specifying other provisions deemed necessary or desirable by the City Attorney.
   (B)   In addition, such written agreement shall specify that the private
property owner shall assure:
      (1)   That the installation of the artwork will be done in a manner which
will protect the artwork and the public;
      (2)   That the artwork will be maintained in good condition; and
      (3)   That insurance and indemnification will be provided as is
appropriate.
(Prior Code, § 14-316) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.31 DISPLAY OF ART IN PUBLIC PLACES.
   (A)   Artwork selected and implemented pursuant to the provisions of this
subchapter may be placed in, on or about any public place or, by agreement with
the owner thereof, any private property with substantial public exposure in and
around the city. Artwork owned by the city may also be loaned for exhibition
elsewhere, upon such terms and conditions as deemed necessary by the Committee.
   (B)   City officials responsible for the design and construction of public
improvements in the city shall make appropriate space available for the
placement of artwork, in consultation with the Committee. The Committee shall
advise the department responsible for the particular public improvement of the
Committee’s decision regarding the design, execution and placement of artwork
in connection with such project. For any proposed artwork requiring an
extraordinary operation or maintenance expense, the Committee shall obtain
prior written approval of the department head responsible for such operation or
maintenance before approving the same.
   (C)   Whenever feasible, installation, maintenance, alteration, refinishing
and moving of artwork shall be done in consultation with the artist.
   (D)   The Committee shall maintain a detailed record of all artwork,
including site drawings, photographs, designs, names of artists and names of
architects whenever feasible. The Committee shall attempt to give appropriate
recognition to the artists and publicity and promotion regarding artwork.
(Prior Code, § 14-317) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.32 OWNERSHIP AND MAINTENANCE OF ARTWORK.
   (A)   All artwork acquired with funds from the Art in Public Places Fund,
with city funds or with grants procured by the city, or by donation pursuant to
this subchapter, §§
35.27 or
35.28, shall be acquired in the name of, and title shall be held by, the city.
   (B)   All artwork placed on the private property pursuant to §§
35.25 and
35.26 shall remain the property of the applicant; the obligation to provide all
maintenance necessary to preserve the artwork in good condition shall remain
with the owner of the site.
      (1)   Maintenance of artwork shall include without limitation:
preservation of the artwork in good condition to the satisfaction of the
Committee; protection of the artwork against physical defacement, mutilation or
alteration; and securing and maintaining insurance to be determined by the
city.
      (2)   In addition to all other remedies provided by law, in the event the
owner fails to maintain the artwork, upon reasonable notice, the city may
perform all necessary repairs, maintenance or secure insurance, and the costs
therefor shall become a lien against the real property.
(Prior Code, § 14-318) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.33 REMOVAL OR ALTERATION OF ARTWORK.
   Artwork installed on or integrated into a construction project pursuant to
the provisions of this chapter shall not be removed or altered without the
approval of the City Council. If such artwork is knowingly removed or altered
without prior approval, the city may pursue any available civil or criminal
remedies or penalties.
(Prior Code, § 14-319) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
§ 35.34 EXEMPTIONS.
   The following are exempt from the provisions of this chapter:
   (A)   All artwork in the collections of, or on display at, or under the
auspices of, the High Plains Heritage Center, City Public Library or Black
Hills State University; and
   (B)   All artwork on display in private city offices or other areas of city-
owned facilities which are not generally frequented by the public.
(Prior Code, § 14-320) (Ord. 1015, passed 8-15-2005)
