§ 76.01 LIGHTS DISPLAYED.
   (A)   A motor vehicle operated within the city shall, during the period from
a half hour after sunset to a half hour before sunrise and any other time when
there is not sufficient light to render clearly discernible any person on the
highway at a distance of 200 feet ahead shall display at least two lighted
headlamps, one on each side of the front of such motor vehicle.
   (B)   It shall not be necessary to have lights burning when the motor
vehicle is parked.
(Prior Code, § 17-426)
Statutory reference:
   Vehicle lights, see SDCL §§ 32-17-1 and 32-17-4
§ 76.02 BRAKE REQUIREMENTS.
   Every motor vehicle operated within the city shall be provided with adequate
brakes in good working order and sufficient to control such motor vehicle at
all times when same is in use pursuant to SDCL §§ 32-18-1 et seq.
(Prior Code, § 17-427)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL §§ 32-18-1 et seq.
§ 76.03 HORN REQUIRED.
   Every motor vehicle when operated within the city shall be equipped with a
horn in good working order capable of emitting sound audible under normal
conditions from a distance of at least 200 feet.
(Prior Code, § 17-428)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-15-10
§ 76.04 MUFFLERS.
   No person shall drive a motor vehicle on the streets or highways in the city
unless such motor vehicle is equipped with a muffler in good working order and
in constant operation to prevent excessive or unusual noises and an exhaust
system pursuant to SDCL § 32-15-17 to prevent annoying smoke. It shall be
unlawful for any person to use a muffler cutout on any motor vehicle upon the
streets, alleys or highways in the city.

10.99

SNOWMOBILES
§ 77.01 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   SNOWMOBILE. Any engine-driven vehicle of a type which utilizes sled-type
runners, wheels or skis with an endless belt tread or similar means of contact
with the surface upon which it is operated.
(Prior Code, § 17-446)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-20A-1(8)
§ 77.02 COMPLIANCE REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a snowmobile within the city
except in compliance with the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 17-447) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.03 OPERATOR’S LICENSE.
   No snowmobile shall be operated within the city until the driver thereof
shall have in his or her possession a valid driver’s or chauffeur’s license
issued under the motor vehicle law of the state.
(Prior Code, § 17-448) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.04 PERMITTING UNAUTHORIZED PERSON TO DRIVE.
   No person shall authorize or knowingly permit a snowmobile owned by him or
her or under his or her control to be driven on any public highway in violation
of any of the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 17-449) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.05 SAFETY EQUIPMENT AND INSPECTIONS.
   No snowmobile shall be driven on the roadway, street or alley when such
snowmobile is in such unsafe condition as to endanger any person or property.
The City Police Department may at any time, upon reasonable cause to believe
that a snowmobile is unsafe or not equipped as required by this subchapter,
require the driver of such vehicle to stop and submit such vehicle to an
inspection and test with reference thereto as may be appropriate. No person
shall operate any vehicle which has been found unsafe except to return such
snowmobile to his or her residence, place of business or to a garage until the
snowmobile has been placed in proper repair.
(Prior Code, § 17-450) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.06 FLAGGING.
   All snowmobiles shall exhibit a red flag or cloth not less than 12 inches
square and hung or suspended five feet above ground level so that the entire
area thereof is visible from all directions while on any roadway, street or
alley.
(Prior Code, § 17-451)
§ 77.07 BRAKES.
   Every snowmobile shall be equipped with brakes adequate to control the
movement in good working order and in constant operation and equipped to
prevent excessive or unusual noise or annoying smoke.
(Prior Code, § 17-452)
§ 77.08 MUFFLERS.
   Every snowmobile shall be at all times equipped with muffler in good working
order and in constant operation to prevent excessive or unusual noise or
annoying smoke.
(Prior Code, § 17-453)
§ 77.09 LIGHTS.
   A snowmobile in motion during the period of one-half hour after sunset to
one-half hour before sunrise shall display at least one lighted lamp on the
front and one on the rear of the snowmobile; which headlight and taillight
shall be in conformity with the standards set by state law.
(Prior Code, § 17-454)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-20A-10
§ 77.10 PERMITTED OPERATIONS.
   It shall be unlawful to operate snowmobiles and all-terrain vehicles on city
property (except where allowed under this section). This includes public parks,
playgrounds, recreation areas, city campground and parking lots.
Notwithstanding, the City Council can authorize special permission for an event
on city property. This section does not prohibit the use of snowmobiles or all-
terrain vehicles by city officials in the normal course of their official
duties.
(Prior Code, § 17-455) (Ord. 800, passed 5-6-1996) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.11 SPEED RESTRICTED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to operate a snowmobile within the city
at a rate of speed faster than five mph less than the posted speed limit
applicable to other motor vehicles.
(Prior Code, § 17-456) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.12 HOURS OF PERMITTED OPERATION.
   No snowmobile shall be operated within the city between the hours of 9:30
p.m. and 6:00 a.m. except that a driver may drive during this restricted time
when he or she is coming into town to his or her residence or is leaving town
to go to his or her residence or when driving from work to his or her
residence.
(Prior Code, § 17-457) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.13 RULES OF THE ROAD.
   Every operator of a snowmobile shall observe all of the rules of the road
pertaining to vehicles and in addition shall yield the right-of-way to motor
vehicles.
(Prior Code, § 17-458)
BICYCLES
§ 77.25 LIGHTS REQUIRED.
   No bicycle shall be permitted on any street, highway or boulevard of the
city between 30 minutes after sunset and 30 minutes before sunrise without a
headlight visible from the front thereof for not less than 300 feet, nor
without a red taillight or in lieu thereof a reflector attached to and visible
from the rear of such bicycle for a distance of not less than 200 feet.
(Prior Code, § 17-476) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-17-25
§ 77.26 UNAUTHORIZED USE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to take any bicycle for the purpose of
riding or propelling the same within the city without consent of the owner.
(Prior Code, § 17-477) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.27 TRAFFIC REGULATIONS GENERALLY.
   Every person riding or propelling a bicycle upon any street or other public
highway in the city shall observe all traffic rules and regulations applicable
thereto; and shall turn only at intersections, signal for all turns, ride at
the right-hand side of the street or highway, pass to the left when passing
overtaken vehicles and individuals that are slower moving and shall pass
vehicles to the right when meeting.
(Prior Code, § 17-478)
Statutory reference:
   Operation on roadway, see SDCL § 32-20B-5
§ 77.28 TRAFFIC-CONTROL DEVICES.
   Person riding or propelling any bicycle shall observe all traffic signs and
stop at all stop signs.
(Prior Code, § 17-479)
§ 77.29 PASSENGERS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for the driver of any bicycle upon a public street of
the city to carry or permit to be carried any other person upon such bicycle,
unless the bicycle has been designed or modified for the carriage of an
additional person.
(Prior Code, § 17-480) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.30 RIDING ON SIDEWALKS.
   No person shall ride or propel a bicycle upon any public sidewalk within the
city in such a manner as to interfere with any pedestrian thereon.
(Prior Code, § 17-481) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.31 SPEED.
   No bicycle shall be ridden faster than is reasonable and proper, but every
bicycle shall be operated with reasonable regard to the safety of the operator
and other persons upon the sidewalks, streets and other public highways of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 17-482) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.32 RIDING ABREAST.
   No person shall ride or propel a bicycle upon any street or other public
highway in the city abreast of or to the left of more than one other person
riding or propelling a bicycle.
(Prior Code, § 17-483) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 77.33 CLINGING TO VEHICLES.
   No person shall ride or operate a bicycle by holding on, clinging to or
attaching such bicycle in any manner to any other vehicle on any public highway
or street.
(Prior Code, § 17-484) Penalty, see §
10.99
Statutory reference:
   Clinging from motorcycle prohibited, see SDCL § 32-20-6.5
CHAPTER 78: TRAFFIC SCHEDULES
Schedule
      
I.   U-turns
SCHEDULE I. U-TURNS.
   Drivers of all vehicles are prohibited from making what is commonly known as
U-turns; that is, turning vehicles from the direction in which traveling to go
in the opposite direction on the same street, on the following streets.
   (A)   All of Main Street;
   (B)   All of Jackson Boulevard from University Avenue East;
   (C)   On Fifth and Seventh Streets from Jackson Boulevard to Grant Street;
   (D)   On Grant, Hudson and Illinois Streets between Fifth and Seventh
Streets; or
   (E)   Any controlled intersection.
(Prior Code, § 17-150)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 90.001 RUNNING AT LARGE PROHIBITED.
   No owner of any animal shall permit such animal to run at large in the city,
and no animal shall be off the premises of its owner unless restrained upon a
leash and accompanied by its owner or a member of the owner’s immediate family,
except when complying with all rules posted in a designated off-leash area.
(Prior Code, § 5-1) (Ord. 955, passed 5-5-2003) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.002 ABANDONMENT OF ANIMALS PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to abandon any animal upon a public
right-of-way or upon the property of another.
(Prior Code, § 5-2) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.003 CRUELTY TO ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to immoderately beat or wantonly or
maliciously torture or injure any animal in any manner, or to neglect to care
for or feed any animal in his or her care or under his or her control.
(Prior Code, § 5-3) Penalty, see §
90.999
Statutory reference:
   Cruelty to animals generally, see SDCL Ch. 40-1
   Municipal authority to prevent, see SDCL § 9-29-11
§ 90.004 POISONING ANIMALS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully administer poison to any
animal, the property of another or to expose any poisonous substance with
intent that the same shall be taken by such animal.
(Prior Code, § 5-4) Penalty, see §
90.999
Statutory reference:
   Poisoning animals, see SDCL § 40-1-20
§ 90.005 SANITARY CONDITION REQUIRED.
   A building, enclosure or property where any animal is kept shall be
maintained and kept in a clean and sanitary condition.
(Prior Code, § 5-5)
§ 90.006 KEEPING OF FOWL, RABBITS RESTRICTED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep chickens, ducks, geese or other
domestic fowl, livestock or rabbits, in any house, pen, coop or enclosure
situated within 100 feet of any dwelling house or store or other building used
or occupied as the residence of any person or within 100 feet of any church,
school or public building. This section does not permit the raising or keeping
of the animals described where they are prohibited by zoning or other
restrictive ordinances.
(Prior Code, § 5-6) (Ord. 579, passed 9-3-1985) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.007 EXOTIC OR NATIVE WILDLIFE.
   (A)   A person may keep any exotic or native wildlife provided they are kept
in compliance with state game, fish and parks laws, this section and city
ordinances.
   (B)   The owner shall register with the animal control officer his or her
name, address and type of animal kept who shall notify the State Game, Fish and
Parks Department.
   (C)   The animal shall be kept separate from all domestic animals to prevent
breeding and transmission of disease and shall be confined to ensure minimum
contact with human beings. The animal control officer shall inspect the
enclosure to ensure that these terms are met.
   (D)   If any such animal attacks or bites any person, the animal shall be
tested pursuant to SDCL § 40-12-5.
   (E)   The animal control officer or any police officer may confiscate,
impound or destroy any such animal found in violation of this section. The
owner shall pay any impoundment costs and fines.
(Prior Code, § 5-7) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.008 ANIMAL ATTACKS.
   (A)   Application. Any animal that has committed a severe or fatal attack
upon any human being shall be permanently and securely confined or humanely
euthanized after complying with §§
90.075 through
90.080. This section will also apply to any severe or fatal attack on any
animal while the offending animal is at large.
   (B)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      SECURELY CONFINED. Confined in a locked pen or enclosure suitable to
prevent the entry of young children and designed to prevent the animal from
escaping. Such pen must have minimum dimensions of five feet by eight feet and
must have secure sides and a secure top. The sides must be embedded into the
ground no less than two feet if the floor is not concrete. The enclosure shall
provide protection from the elements. Any time the animal is out of the pen it
will be with a responsible adult and on a leash at all times.
      SEVERE INJURY. Any physical injury that results in broken bones or
disfiguring lacerations requiring multiple sutures or cosmetic surgery.
   (C)   Violation. Failure to comply with these guidelines will result in the
animal being impounded and euthanized.
(Prior Code, § 5-8) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.009 DESTRUCTION OF ANIMALS.
   The animal control officer may destroy any sick or injured animal which has
been impounded without holding it for 72 hours if its condition is such that
immediate destruction is necessary or desirable. All animals shall be destroyed
in a humane manner.
(Prior Code, § 5-9)
§ 90.010 RIGHT OF ENTRY OF ANIMAL CONTROL OFFICER.
   (A)   The animal control officer may enter upon the premises where any
animal is kept in a reportedly cruel or inhumane manner and demand to examine
such animal and to take possession of such animal if there is probable cause to
believe the same has been treated inhumanely.
   (B)   The animal control officer is hereby authorized and empowered to enter
upon any enclosure or lot within the city limits, in quest of any animal
suspected of being affected by rabies and to apprehend any animal which has
been observed to be running at large.
(Prior Code, § 5-10)
§ 90.011 LIABILITY; FINES AND COSTS.
   All fees, fines or costs levied or incurred by the city in the enforcement
of this chapter shall be paid by the owner of the animal.
(Prior Code, § 5-11)
§ 90.012 PETS PROHIBITED IN CITY PARK DURING FESTIVAL.
   Domesticated pets shall not be permitted in the city park (Centennial Park)
from 6:00 a.m. Friday until 6:00 p.m. Sunday during the festival in the park.
For the purpose of this section, the city park (Centennial Park) includes the
recreation path through the park, Canyon Street, sidewalks to the east and west
of Canyon Street and the parking lots. This section shall not apply to dogs
used by law enforcement, the disabled or the visually handicapped.
(Prior Code, § 5-12) (Ord. 809, passed 9-16-1996; Ord. 992, passed 9-24-2004;
Ord. 1186, passed 1-6-2014) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.013 UNATTENDED ANIMAL.
   (A)   A person may not leave any animal unattended in a standing or parked
motor vehicle in a manner that endangers the animal’s health or safety.
   (B)   A person found to be in violation of this section shall bear the costs
and fees associated with any required care, treatment, impounding or kenneling
of the animal.
(Prior Code, § 5-13) (Ord. 1249, passed 8-1-2016) Penalty, see §
90.999
DOGS AND CATS
§ 90.025 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AT LARGE. Off the premises of the owner and not under the control of the
owner or a member of his or her immediate family either by leash, cord or
chain.
   CAT. Both male and female members of the feline family.
   DOG. Male and female members of the canine family.
   LEASH. A cord, thong or chain not more than ten feet in length, by which a
dog or cat is controlled by the person accompanying it.
   OWNER. Any person owning, keeping or harboring a dog or cat.
(Prior Code, § 5-31)
§ 90.026 DANGEROUS OR VICIOUS DOGS OR CATS.
   (A)   Dangerous or vicious dogs or cats at large prohibited.
      (1)   No dog or cat of dangerous, vicious or fierce propensities or
tendencies may be at large at any time within the limits of the city. It shall
be unlawful for the owner or other person having any such dog or cat in his or
her possession or under his or her control or in any manner keeping or
harboring any such dog or cat within the limits of the city, to cause or permit
any such dog or cat to be at large.
      (2)   If any dog bites or attempts to bite any person while such dog or
cat is at large, then such dog or cat shall be conclusively presumed to be a
dangerous dog or cat and dog or cat of dangerous propensities and tendencies.
      (3)   If any dog or cat attacks or attempts to attack any animal or
chases or otherwise attempts to catch a person, such dog or cat shall be
conclusively presumed to be vicious and to have vicious propensities and
tendencies.
(Prior Code, § 5-32)
   (B)   Destruction of dangerous, vicious dogs and cats. Any dangerous or
vicious dog or cat or a dog or cat having dangerous or vicious propensities and
tendencies found at large after the owner has previous knowledge or notice that
such dog or cat is dangerous or vicious or has dangerous or vicious
propensities and tendencies may be killed by any police officer of the city
without such officer having to catch or impound such dog or cat.
(Prior Code, § 5-33)
   (C)   Destruction of biting, scratching dogs. Any dog or cat having bitten,
scratched or attacked two or more persons off the premises of the owner shall
be destroyed by the Police Department.
(Prior Code, § 5-35)
§ 90.027 NUISANCES.
   Any dog or cat within the city which habitually barks or howls or chases or
annoys animals, vehicles or persons or which damages or destroys property is
hereby declared a nuisance. The Chief of Police or other police officer may
proceed to abate such nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 5-34)
§ 90.028 CLEANING UP AFTER PETS REQUIRED.
   The owner, keeper, caretaker or attendant of any animal, canine or feline,
shall immediately and thoroughly clean up any fecal matter deposited by said
animal on any property not owned by the owner, keeper, caretaker or attendant.
(Prior Code, § 5-36) (Ord. 778, passed 8-7-1995) Penalty, see §
90.999
LICENSING
§ 90.040 LICENSE REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person within the city to keep, maintain or
have in his or her custody or under his or her control any dog or cat without
first having obtained a license from the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-51) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.041 APPLICATION.
   Any person desiring to keep, maintain or have in his or her custody or
control any dog or cat shall on or before January 1 in each year make
application to the animal control officer for a license to keep such dog or
cat. Such application shall be in writing stating the name, sex, color and
other distinguishing characteristics of such dog or cat and the name and
address of the applicant.
(Prior Code, § 5-52)
§ 90.042 RABIES VACCINATION REQUIRED.
   Before any license shall be issued under this subchapter, the applicant
shall furnish a certificate of rabies vaccination issued by a veterinarian
licensed to practice within this state evidencing vaccination of the dog or cat
for which the license is desired has been vaccinated against rabies and that
such vaccination will be good for the license year.
(Prior Code, § 5-53)
§ 90.043 FEE; DURATION.
   (A)   Fee. Before any license shall be issued under the provision of this
subchapter, the applicant shall pay a license fee as follows:
      (1)   Each neutered male or spayed female dog or cat: $ 5; and
      (2)   Each unspayed female or not neutered male dog or cat: $10.
(Prior Code, § 5-54)
   (B)   Duration. Every license issued under this subchapter shall be valid
from January 1 until the December 31 next following.
(Prior Code, § 5-55)
(Ord. 854, passed 12-21-1998)
§ 90.044 TAGS REQUIRED.
   (A)   Issuance of tag. It shall be the duty of the animal control officer at
the time of the issuance of a license under this subchapter to furnish and
deliver to the applicant for such license, a tag for each dog or cat for which
such license is issued. The number of the license and the year for which such
license is issued shall be stamped or engraved on the tag.
(Prior Code, § 5-56)
   (B)   Replacement of tag. In the event of the loss of any tag issued under
the provision of this subchapter, the animal control officer is hereby
authorized to issue another tag upon payment of the actual cost of the tag upon
application being made and upon satisfactory proof that such tag has been lost.
(Prior Code, § 5-57)
   (C)   Dog or cat to wear tag. It shall be the duty of the owner of the dog
or cat licensed under this subchapter to place a collar around the neck of such
dog or cat, on which collar shall be securely fastened the tag furnished by the
animal control officer.
(Prior Code, § 5-58)
IMPOUNDMENT
§ 90.055 AUTHORIZED.
   (A)   Any dog or cat found in violation of the provisions of this chapter
may be seized and impounded by any police officer or animal control officer or
any other person at their direction.
   (B)   Impoundment may be in any animal shelter designated by the Council.
(Prior Code, § 5-76)
§ 90.056 NOTICE TO OWNER.
   The owner of any dog or cat impounded under the provisions of this
subchapter, if his or her identity and location can be obtained by reasonable
means, shall be notified within 24 hours that his or her dog or cat has been
impounded.
(Prior Code, § 5-77)
§ 90.057 FINES AND FEES.
   (A)   The fine charged for the impoundment of any dog or cat under the
provision of this subchapter shall be:
      (1)   Thirty dollars for the first impoundment; and
      (2)   Fifty dollars for the second and any subsequent impoundment.
   (B)   A $20 per day boarding fee shall also be added to the impoundment fine
for the first and each subsequent day that the animal is housed by the city.
(Prior Code, § 5-78) (Ord. 611, passed 2-17-1987; Ord. 937, passed 10-21-2002)
§ 90.058 HOLDING, REDEMPTION OF UNVACCINATED, UNLICENSED DOGS AND CATS.
   (A)   Any dog or cat impounded under this subchapter shall be held in the
animal shelter designated by the city for a period of 120 hours. The owner of
any dog or cat impounded may redeem such animal by paying the impoundment fee
within 120 hours of the impoundment. The owner of any impounded dog or cat
which has been vaccinated or licensed under this chapter upon satisfactory
proof of ownership and after paying the impoundment fee may redeem his or her
dog or cat. The owner of an unvaccinated or unlicensed dog or cat shall be
required to secure a certificate of vaccination and city license within 120
hours before being released after paying all fees.
   (B)   In no event shall any impounded animal be returned to the owner until
the owner has produced a current license or receipt therefor and evidence of
current vaccination and paid the fee for impoundment.
(Prior Code, § 5-79) (Ord. 785, passed 11-6-1995)
§ 90.059 REDEMPTION BY PERSON OTHER THAN OWNER.
   If the owner of any dog or cat impounded under this subchapter shall fail to
redeem such dog or cat within 120 hours after such impoundment, the city’s
liability for such dog or cat shall cease. Any other person may upon complying
with the provisions of this subchapter, redeem such dog or cat from the shelter
and be the lawful owner of such dog or cat thereafter.
(Prior Code, § 5-80) (Ord. 785, passed 11-6-1995)
§ 90.060 DISPOSITION OF UNREDEEMED DOGS AND CATS.
   All dogs and cats impounded under this subchapter and which have not been
redeemed or purchased as authorized by this subchapter within 120 hours of such
impoundment may be adopted by any person or disposed of in a humane manner by
any police officer or animal control officer of the city or by any
veterinarian.
(Prior Code, § 5-81) (Ord. 785, passed 11-6-1995)
RABIES CONTROL
§ 90.075 REPORT OF BITES.
   (A)   Every person having knowledge that an animal has bitten or is
suspected of biting a human being, shall forthwith report the same to the
animal control officer for disposition of such animal under the provisions of
this subchapter. Every person bitten by an animal shall promptly report it to
the animal control officer.
   (B)   The animal shall thereupon be securely quarantined at the discretion
of the animal control officer for a period of not less than ten days.
(Prior Code, § 5-101)
§ 90.076 QUARANTINE OF ANIMAL.
   (A)   The animal ordered to be quarantined shall not be released from such
quarantine except by written permission of the animal control officer. Such
quarantine may be at the city’s animal shelter or at the owner’s option, in a
veterinary hospital of his or her choice located in the city. The expenses of
quarantine shall be paid by the owner. In the case of stray animals or in the
cases of animals whose ownership is not known, such quarantine shall be at the
shelter designated as the city’s animal shelter.
   (B)   The owner, upon demand made by the animal control officer shall
forthwith place in the custody of a licensed veterinarian, any animal which has
bitten a human, or which is suspected as having been exposed to rabies, for
supervised quarantine. The expense of such quarantine shall be borne by the
owner. The animal may be reclaimed by the owner if found to be free of rabies.
(Prior Code, § 5-102)
§ 90.077 DIAGNOSES.
   When an animal under quarantine has been diagnosed as being rabid or
suspected by a licensed veterinarian as being rabid and dies while under such
observation, the animal control officer shall immediately send the head of such
animal to a competent laboratory for pathological examination. The animal
control officer shall notify the proper public health officers of reports of
human contacts with such animal and the diagnosis made on the animal.
(Prior Code, § 5-103)
§ 90.078 AREA QUARANTINE.
   (A)   When one or both reports give a positive diagnosis of rabies, the
animal control officer may recommend the animal be area quarantined for a
period of 30 days. Upon the invocation of such quarantine, no animal shall be
taken into such area during such period of quarantine.
   (B)   Every unvaccinated animal bitten by an animal showing positive
symptoms of rabies shall be forthwith destroyed or shall be held under
quarantine not less than six weeks at the owner’s option and expense.
(Prior Code, § 5-104)
§ 90.079 EXTENSION.
   If there are additional positive cases of rabies occurring during the period
of the quarantine, such period of quarantine may be extended for an additional
six months.
(Prior Code, § 5-105)
§ 90.080 DESTRUCTION OF ANIMALS.
   No person shall kill or cause to be killed any rabid animal, or any animal
biting a human, except as herein provided, or remove such animal from the city
limits without written permission from the animal control officer. The carcass
of any dead animal exposed to rabies shall, upon demand, be surrendered to the
animal control officer. The animal control officer shall direct the disposition
of any animal found to be infected with rabies. No person shall fail or refuse
to surrender any animal quarantined or fail or refuse to destroy an animal as
required herein when such demand is made by the animal control officer.
(Prior Code, § 5-106) Penalty, see §
90.999
§ 90.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   A violation of §
90.013 is a Class 2 misdemeanor carrying a $200 fine.
(Prior Code, § 5-13) (Ord. 1249, passed 8-1-2016)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 91.01 BURNING PROHIBITED.
   Open burning that is offensive or objectionable because of smoke or odor
emissions or when atmospheric conditions or local circumstances make such fires
hazardous shall be prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 7-1) (Ord. 1067, passed 8-20-2007) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.02 FALSE FIRE ALARMS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to give a false alarm or false report of
a fire.
(Prior Code, § 7-2) Penalty, see §
91.99
Statutory reference:
   False fire alarms, see SDCL § 22-11-9
§ 91.03 SALE OR DISCHARGE OF FIREWORKS.
   (A)   No person may sell or cause to be sold, discharged or caused to be
discharged, any pyrotechnics or fireworks of any description whatsoever within
the city.
   (B)   An exception to this section is the discharge of fireworks as part of
a professional display operated by a licensed pyrotechnic operator under the
procedure set forth in the International Fire Code, as amended from time to
time.
(Prior Code, § 7-3) (Ord. 545, passed 8-15-1983; Ord. 1273, passed 3-19-2018)
Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.04 BURN PERMIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   (1)   Notwithstanding §
91.01, the burning of slash may be permitted in rural service districts upon
the issuance of a burn permit by the Public Works Administrator, subject to the
terms and conditions contained in the permit.
      (2)   No permit shall be issued except upon proper application in a form
prescribed by the city.
   (B)   Any permit issued under this section shall require an inspection of
the proposed burn site and the surrounding area and notification to the Fire
Chief of the date, time and location of the proposed burn.
(Prior Code, § 7-4) (Ord. 919, passed 4-1-2002; Ord. 1061, passed 7-16-2007)
§ 91.05 BURNING OF BUILDING OR STRUCTURE FOR TRAINING PURPOSES.
   The Chief of the Fire Department may permit the burning of any suitable
building or structure for Fire Department training purposes with the permission
of the owner provided that the burning of any building or structure pursuant to
this section shall be conducted in a manner approved by the Fire Chief.
(Prior Code, § 7-5) (Ord. 979, passed 3-19-2004)
§ 91.06 OPEN BURNING.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      BRANDING IRON BURNER. A stove, furnace or device constructed of non-
combustible materials used to heat irons for the purpose of branding livestock,
fueled by cut or split wood or liquid fuel and constructed so that the heat
source is contained in such a manner that sparks or embers are not allowed to
freely escape into the open atmosphere and located not closer than 15 feet from
any combustible surface and continually attended.
      CAMPFIRE. A campground or backyard type fire that has a maximum fuel area
of three feet, without screening. A CAMPFIRE may be fueled by cut or split wood
or liquid fuel and must be located not closer than 15 feet from any combustible
surface and continually attended.
      CAMPGROUND. Any commercial campground that is permitted by the city, the
state or the United States Forest Service that is operated by said agency or
private individuals or corporations.
      CHARCOAL GRILL. A metal or stone device not resting on the ground with a
metal grate designed to cook food using charcoal briquettes.
      LIQUID FUEL GRILL. A metal or stone device designed to cook food using
gaseous combustible fuel.
      OPEN FIRE. Any outdoor fire. OPEN FIRE shall not include charcoal grills,
outdoor fireplaces, liquid fuel grills or branding iron burners as defined
herein.
      OUTDOOR FIREPLACE. A manufactured appliance constructed of non-
combustible materials, with a maximum fuel area of three feet, constructed to
include a screen, chimney or other device placed above the fuel area so that
the heat source is contained in such a manner that sparks or embers are not
allowed to freely escape into the open atmosphere. An OUTDOOR FIREPLACE may be
fueled by cut or split wood or liquid fuel and must be located not closer than
15 feet from any combustible surface and continually attended.
   (B)   Regulations.
      (1)   Open fire. No person shall set an open fire within the city when
the National Weather Service has declared the Grassland Fire Danger Index to be
in the “high,” “very high” or “extreme” category within the city. Use of an
open fire is allowed only when the Grassland Fire Index falls in the “moderate”
category or below. The prohibition against open fire, as provided herein, shall
automatically be suspended during any time period the Grassland Fire Danger
Index falls below the “high” category within the city.
      (2)   Campgrounds. The ban on open burning (open fire) does not apply to
those designated areas of any commercial, city, state or federal campground
that is permitted by the city except when the National Weather Service has
declared the Grassland Fire Danger Index to be in the “extreme” category within
the city or unless otherwise specifically banned by a resolution of the City
Council.
      (3)   Burn permits. A permit is required for any open burning which
includes the purpose of land clearing.
(Prior Code, § 7-6) (Ord. 1159, passed 7-16-2012) Penalty, see §
91.99
FIRE PREVENTION CODE
§ 91.20 INTERNATIONAL FIRE CODE ADOPTED.
   The Common Council hereby adopts the 2021 International Fire Code as
published by the International Code Council, including appendix B, C and D. A
copy of the Code shall be on file in the office of the City Building Official.
(Prior Code, § 7-46) (Ord. 878, passed 4-3-2000; Ord. 989, passed 8-20-2004;
Ord. 1064, passed 7-2-2007; Ord. 1126, passed 10-4-2010; Ord. 1170, passed 1-
22-2013; Ord. 1230, passed 2-1-2016; Ord. 1298, passed 2-4-2019; Ord. 1349,
passed 11-15-2021)
§ 91.21 CONFLICTS.
   In the event of any conflict between the provisions of the code adopted in §
91.20 and applicable provisions of this code, state law or city ordinance, the
provisions of this code, state law or city ordinance shall prevail and be
controlling.
(Prior Code, § 7-47) (Ord. 1298, passed 2-4-2019)
§ 91.22 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of the code adopted in §
91.20, the following definition shall apply unless the context clearly
indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MUNICIPALITY. The City of Spearfish.
(Prior Code, § 7-48)
§ 91.23 EXPLOSIVES; BLASTING AGENTS; HAZARDOUS CHEMICALS.
   (A)   Storage of explosives, blasting agents. The limits referred to in the
Fire Prevention Code adopted in §
91.20, in which storage of explosives and blasting agents is prohibited, shall
be as established by the Common Council.
(Prior Code, § 7-49)
   (B)   Routes for vehicles transporting explosives. The routes referred to in
the Fire Prevention Code adopted in §
91.20 for vehicles transporting explosives and blasting agents shall be as
established by the Fire Chief and the Chief of Police.
(Prior Code, § 7-50)
   (C)   Routes for vehicles transporting hazardous chemicals. The routes
referred to in the Fire Prevention Code adopted in §
91.20 for vehicles transporting hazardous chemicals and other dangerous
articles shall be as established by the Fire Chief and Chief of Police.
(Prior Code, § 7-51) Penalty, see §
91.99
§ 91.24 FIRE LANES.
   The fire lanes referred to in the Fire Prevention Code adopted in §
91.20 shall be as established by the Fire Chief and Chief of Police.
(Prior Code, § 7-52)
§ 91.25 ADDITIONAL MODIFICATIONS.
   (A)   The Chief of the Fire Department shall have power to modify any of the
provisions of the Fire Prevention Code adopted in §
91.20 upon application in writing by the owner or lessee, or his or her duly
authorized agent, when there are practical difficulties in the way of carrying
out the strict letter of the code, provided that the spirit of the code shall
be observed, public safety secured and substantial justice done.
   (B)   The particulars of such modification, when granted or allowed, and the
decision of the Chief of the Fire Department thereon, shall be entered upon the
records of the Department and a signed copy shall be furnished to the
applicant.
(Prior Code, § 7-53)
§ 91.26 APPEALS.
   Whenever the Chief of the Fire Department shall disapprove an application or
refuse to grant a permit applied for or when it is claimed that the provisions
of the code adopted in §
91.20 do not apply or that the true intent and meaning of the code have been
misconstrued or wrongly interpreted, the applicant may appeal from the decision
of the Chief of the Fire Department to the Common Council within 30 days from
the date of the decision appealed.
(Prior Code, § 7-54)
§ 91.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   (1)   Violation of §
91.06 will be punished by a fine of $100. Any violator of this section shall
also be subject to the suppression costs of extinguishing a fire.
      (2)   Nothing herein shall be construed to prohibit or supersede any
civil remedy otherwise available to any person or entity.
      (3)   The permissibility of the ignition of any fire as specified herein
shall not operate to relieve the igniter of any duty of care otherwise imposed
by law; nor shall this section operate to absolve any person of any liability
for damages to persons or property which may occur as a result of the fire.
(Prior Code, § 7-6) (Ord. 1159, passed 7-16-2012)
CHAPTER 92: HEALTH AND SANITATION; NUISANCES

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 92.01 UNWHOLESOME FOOD, DRINK.
   No meat, fish, game fowl, fruit, milk, vegetables, ice or any other article
of food or drink intended for human consumption, the same being then stale,
unhealthy, unsound, tainted, putrid or unwholesome, shall be sold, bartered or
kept for barter or sale in any public or private market, store, shop or place
within the city or peddled on streets.
(Prior Code, § 9-1) Penalty, see §
92.99
NUISANCES
§ 92.15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   GRASS AND WEEDS. Includes, but is not limited to, Bermuda grass, centipede
grass, fescue, rye grass, blue grass, western wheat species, buffalo grass,
grama grass, needle and thread, green needle and any weeds and any volunteer
woody plant material and other noxious or unhealthful vegetation. This does not
include trees, shrubs, landscaped ornamental grasses and flower, fruit or
vegetable gardens.
   NATURAL AREA. Uncultivated and unseeded land, still in a state of nature.
Any growth on land, once it has been cleared or plowed, is not a NATURAL AREA,
even though it has not been planted or cultivated by anyone.
   NOXIOUS MATTER. Trash, garbage and all other material which has been strewn
about or otherwise apparently abandoned, or of no apparent value, which is
unsightly, or which may be potentially hazardous as a breeding ground for
insects and rodents and other undesirable animals, or which may prove hazardous
to individuals using the area upon which these NOXIOUS MATTERS exist.
   PASTURELAND. Land covered with grass or herbage and suitable for cutting hay
or grazing by domesticated livestock, such as horses, cattle, sheep or swine.
(Prior Code, § 9-26) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
Statutory reference:
   Abatement of nuisances, see SDCL § 9-29-13
   Power to promote health and suppression of diseases, see SDCL Ch. 9-32
   Remedies against nuisances, see SDCL Ch. 21-10
§ 92.16 DECLARED; PROHIBITED.
   (A)   No person may create, maintain or commit, or permit to be created,
maintained or committed, any nuisance as defined in division (B) below or as
enumerated in division (C) below.
   (B)   For the purpose of this section, a NUISANCE is doing any act without
lawful authority or failure to perform an act, which act or omission:
      (1)   Annoys, injures or endangers the comfort, repose, health or safety
of others; or
      (2)   Interferes with, obstructs or tends to obstruct or renders
dangerous for passage any body of water including streams, creeks, rivers,
canals, lakes, ponds or basins, or any public park, square, street, right-of-
way or highway.
   (C)   Nuisances include, but are not limited to, the following:
      (1)   Junk, litter, debris, rubbish, building materials, lumber, vehicle
parts, appliances, furniture, yard waste, noxious matter and other debris in
view of adjacent properties or public rights-of-way. On construction sites, it
is the responsibility of the owner or general contractor to have a container
for all construction debris. Any complaint of blowing debris from construction
sites may result in immediate resolution by the city;
      (2)   Wrecked, dismantled, inoperative, junked, partially dismantled or
unlicensed motor vehicles, or the parts thereof, disassembled bicycles and
bicycle parts or other mechanical machines or parts when the items are stored,
collected, piled or otherwise kept without being screened from view;
      (3)   Grass and weeds having reached a height of ten inches or any
noxious weeds. The following areas may be exempt from the ten-inch height
limit:
         (a)   Regional drainage ponds or regional drainage ditches which
convey or store storm water or irrigation ditches;
         (b)   Marshes, wetlands, riverbanks, creek banks or coulees;
         (c)   Areas within 20 feet of a creek or stream;
         (d)   Areas with a slope that is at or steeper than two horizontal
feet to one vertical foot;
         (e)   Natural areas;
         (f)   Public parks or greenway tracts;
         (g)   Golf courses;
         (h)   Areas that are highly erodible; or
         (i)   Pastureland.
      (4)   Any portion of a sidewalk that has not been cleared of ice or snow
within 48 hours of the termination of any snow or ice event. The property
owner, agent or occupant of the property abutting the sidewalk is responsible
for ensuring the sidewalk is cleared of ice or snow;
      (5)   Obstructions on any portion of a sidewalk including an overhead
clearance of less than ten feet above the sidewalk:
         (a)   The property owner, agent or occupant of the property abutting
the sidewalk is responsible for ensuring the sidewalk is cleared of any
obstructions; and
         (b)   Property owners, agents or occupants are also responsible for
ensuring the sidewalks have a minimum clearance of ten feet over the sidewalk.
      (6)   Any sidewalk that is in disrepair as determined by city staff; and
      (7)   Any other condition the Common Council declares to be a nuisance.
(Prior Code, § 9-27) (Ord. 951, passed 4-21-2003; Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
Penalty, see §
92.99
Statutory reference:
   Authority to require snow removal, see SDCL §§ 9-30-5
§ 92.17 NOTICE.
   (A)   The designated city official will notify the property owner, agent or
occupant creating, permitting or maintaining a nuisance to remedy or abate the
nuisance on the property. The notice and order to abate will be in writing and
may be hand delivered or sent by certified mail, return receipt requested to
the property owner, agent or occupant at his or her last known address. The
notice will order the owner, agent or occupant to remedy or abate the nuisance
within a designated number of days from the date the notice was hand delivered
or postmarked. Nothing in this section prevents the city from attempting to
informally resolve the nuisance by contacting the property owner, agent or
occupant, informing them of the nuisance and requesting they abate it.
   (B)   This section does not apply to nuisances caused by the failure of a
property owner, agent or occupant to remove snow or ice from the sidewalk.
(Prior Code, § 9-29) (Ord. 951, passed 4-21-2003; Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 92.18 NOTICE FOR SIDEWALK SNOW AND ICE.
   If a property owner, agent or occupant creates, maintains or commits, or
permits to be created, maintained or committed a nuisance by failing to remove
snow or ice from the sidewalk, the designated city official will notify the
property owner, agent or occupant by calling them or placing a door hanger on
the property. If the snow or ice is not removed within 24 hours of the call or
placement of the door hanger, the city may provide for the abatement of the
nuisance in accordance with §
92.19.
(Prior Code, § 9-30) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.19 ABATEMENT.
   (A)   If a property owner, agent or occupant fails, after receiving written
notice, to abate the nuisance within the time allowed, the designated city
official is hereby authorized and empowered to provide for the abatement of the
nuisance.
   (B)   Upon completing the abatement, all related receipts and administrative
costs will be billed to the owner, agent or occupant. If full payment is not
received from the owner, agent or occupant within 30 days, the city may tax the
cost of the abatement and administrative costs by special assessment against
the real property on which the nuisance occurred or, in the case of sidewalks,
against the real property abutting or adjoining the sidewalk. Administrative
costs shall be set by resolution and are applicable to any nuisance that is
abated by the city or its designee.
(Prior Code, § 9-31) (Ord. 951, passed 4-21-2003; Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 92.20 ALTERNATE ABATEMENT PROCEDURE.
   In addition to any method of abatement of nuisances within the city provided
by the provisions of this subchapter, any nuisance found within the city may be
abated in the manner provided by state law.
(Prior Code, § 9-32) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 92.21 RECOVERY OF EXPENSES.
   The city may recover the expenses incurred in abating any nuisance under the
provisions of this subchapter from the person creating, permitting or
maintaining the same in a civil suit instituted for such purpose.
(Prior Code, § 9-33) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 92.22 APPEALS.
   (A)   A person who is the subject of a nuisance notice and order to abate
may appeal the order to the Common Council by submitting a written appeal. The
number of days the person has to appeal will be designated in the notice
received pursuant to §
92.17. The written appeal must be submitted to city administration at 625 N.
Fifth Street, Spearfish, South Dakota, 57783.
   (B)   This section does not apply to nuisances caused by the failure of a
property owner, agent or occupant to remove snow or ice from the sidewalk.
(Prior Code, § 9-34) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 92.23 VEGETATION ON CITY PROPERTY.
   No person by use of biological, chemical, mechanical or other means may
alter vegetation on city property. A violation of this section is subject to
the general penalty provision as set forth in §
92.99. In addition, the city may recover costs of restoring the property to its
original state or replacing the altered vegetation.
(Prior Code, § 9-36) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020) Penalty, see §
92.99
§ 92.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   In addition to the abatement remedies prescribed in this code, any
person convicted of maintaining any nuisance in violation of any provision of
this code shall be punished as prescribed in §
10.99, unless otherwise specifically provided, and a separate offense shall be
deemed committed on each day during or on which a violation occurs or
continues.
(Prior Code, § 9-35) (Ord. 1328, passed 9-21-2020)

§ 93.01 DETERMINATION OF ABANDONMENT.
   Whenever any vehicle is left unattended on any public street, alley way or
parking lot within the city for a longer period than 24 hours without notifying
the Chief of Police where such vehicle is parked, it shall be deemed to be an
abandoned vehicle and subject to the provisions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 17-501)
§ 93.02 VEHICLES BLOCKING TRAFFIC, WRECKED VEHICLES.
   A vehicle found unattended upon a bridge or causeway or on the traveled
portion of any street where such vehicle constitutes an obstruction and hazard
to traffic or a vehicle which appears to have sustained reportable accident
damage may be removed at any time and without regard to the 24-hour period
provided for in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 17-502)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-30-14
§ 93.03 REMOVAL.
   Whenever any police officer finds an abandoned vehicle within the city, he
or she is hereby authorized to provide for the removal of such vehicle to the
nearest garage or place of safety.
(Prior Code, § 17-503)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-30-13
§ 93.04 NOTICE TO OWNER.
   It shall be the duty of the Police Department to notify by certified mail
the registered owner and if encumbered, the lien holder shall also be notified
of the removal and storage of any vehicle under the provisions of this chapter
and where such vehicle has been stored and that the registered owner of the
vehicle may recover the vehicle upon the payment of all costs incident to the
removal and storage of such vehicle.
(Prior Code, § 17-504)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-30-15
§ 93.05 SALE OF UNCLAIMED VEHICLE.
   If, after three months from the date of mailing the notice of removal and
storage provided for by this chapter the vehicle shall remain unclaimed, such
vehicle may be sold by the Police Department at public auction upon notice to
be published in a newspaper of general circulation in the county not less than
once a week for two consecutive weeks.
(Prior Code, § 17-505)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL Ch. 32-36
§ 93.06 NOTICE OF SALE.
   The notice of sale provided for by this chapter shall contain a description
of the removed and stored vehicle, including the year, make, model, serial
number, color, license number, if any, a statement that the vehicle was found
abandoned, the date thereof and the place, date and time at which such vehicle
shall be sold, which date shall not be sooner than one week following the date
of the last publication of notice.
(Prior Code, § 17-506)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL Ch. 32-36
§ 93.07 DISPOSITION OF FUNDS FROM SALE.
   After the costs of removing, storing, advertising and selling a vehicle
under the provisions of this chapter are deducted, the balance of the funds
derived from the sale of such vehicle under this chapter shall be held for the
owner of such vehicle for a period of 90 days. If such proceeds are not claimed
at the expiration of such 90-day period, such proceeds shall be paid into the
General Fund of the city.
(Prior Code, § 17-507)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL Ch. 32-36
§ 93.08 LIEN FOR COSTS.
   The Police Department shall have a possessory lien upon any vehicle removed
under the provisions of this chapter for the costs in taking custody of and
storing such vehicle.
(Prior Code, § 17-508)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL § 32-30-18
§ 93.09 TITLE MAY VEST IN CITY.
   If, after six months from the date of mailing the notice of removal and
storage provided for by this chapter, the vehicle shall remain unclaimed, the
title to such vehicle shall be vested in the city, and such vehicle may be
disposed of in any manner as may be provided by the Common Council. The
proceeds of any such disposal shall first be applied to the costs incurred in
the enforcement of this chapter with the balance to be deposited to the General
Fund of the city.
(Prior Code, § 17-509)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL Ch. 32-36
§ 93.10 NOTICE TO COMMISSIONER OF VEHICLES.
   Within 30 days after acquiring title to any vehicle under the provisions of
this chapter, the Common Council shall notify the Department of Commerce and
Regulation thereof and shall provide the Department of Commerce and Regulation
on such form as it may prescribe, all facts and information relevant thereto as
it may require. Upon receipt thereof, the Department of Commerce and Regulation
shall notify the owner of record at his or her last known address of the
actions taken.
(Prior Code, § 17-510)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see SDCL Ch. 32-36
CHAPTER 94: ASSEMBLIES, PARADES AND PROCESSIONS
Section
   
94.01   Permit required
   
94.02   Application for permit
   
94.03   Contents of permit
   
94.04   Matters considered in determining issuance of permit
   
94.05   Issuance

§ 94.01 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to organize or hold or participate in
any parade, meeting, assembly, outdoor concert or procession of persons and/or
vehicles on the streets, sidewalks or public parks of this city unless such
activity shall have first been authorized by a written permit issued by the
Chief of Police therefor.
(Prior Code, § 14-101) (Ord. 746, passed 10-4-1993; Ord. 835, passed 11-17-
1997) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.02 APPLICATION FOR PERMIT.
   The application for a permit required by this chapter shall contain the
following:
   (A)   The name and address of the applicant;
   (B)   The name and address of the person the applicant represents;
   (C)   The exact time and date of commencement and termination of each act or
activity desired;
   (D)   The purpose, location and route of such act or activity, if
applicable;
   (E)   The person, group, association or body to be authorized under the
permit to do such act or activity and the number of persons to participate;
   (F)   The age of any minors who may participate in such activity and the
name of the person who will be responsible for such minors; and
   (G)   Such other relevant information as the Chief of Police may require for
the investigation of the applicant.
(Prior Code, § 14-102)
§ 94.03 CONTENTS OF PERMIT.
   Upon issuance of a permit required by this chapter, the same shall contain
therein all information contained in the application therefor and be signed by
the Chief of Police and a signed copy of the same shall be kept with the
application, both on file in the office of the Chief of Police.
(Prior Code, § 14-103)
§ 94.04 MATTERS CONSIDERED IN DETERMINING ISSUANCE OF PERMIT.
   In deciding whether to issue a permit under the provisions of this chapter,
the Chief of Police shall consider:
   (A)   Number of persons to participate;
   (B)   Anticipated traffic conditions at the time and date proposed for the
activity;
   (C)   Schedule of other similar activities for which permits may have been
issued;
   (D)   Adequacy of adult supervision for any minors scheduled to participate;
   (E)   Availability of city personnel whose presence on duty may be required
by the activity and by the necessity to protect the general public; and
   (F)   Adequacy of public facilities in the location proposed for the
activity to accommodate the proposed activity and the normal public use of
public facilities in the proposed location.
(Prior Code, § 14-104)
§ 94.05 ISSUANCE.
   The permit required by the provisions of this chapter shall be issued by the
Chief of Police upon application therefor; provided, however, that such permit
may be denied or refused if it shall appear that the applicant therefor or the
act or activity requested by such application shall violate any applicable
provision of this code, state law or city ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 14-105)
§ 94.06 TIME LAPSE BETWEEN APPLICATION, ACTIVITY.
   It shall be unlawful for any activity authorized under this chapter to
commence within five days from the date of the application therefor.
(Prior Code, § 14-106) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.07 DEVIATION FROM PERMIT.
   It shall be unlawful for any person participating in any act or activity for
which a permit has been granted under the provisions of this chapter to deviate
from or alter any of the terms or contents of such permit.
(Prior Code, § 14-107) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.08 DISPLAY OF PERMIT.
   Every person having a permit issued under the provisions of this chapter
shall have such permit in his or her possession during the activity permitted
thereby and shall display such permit upon the request of any law enforcement
officer. Failure to display such permit shall be deemed a misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-108) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.09 REVOCATION OF PERMIT.
   Any permit issued under the provisions of this chapter may be revoked by the
Chief of Police for the violation by the permittee of any applicable provision
of this code, state law or city ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 14-109)
§ 94.10 DISPERSAL OF ACTIVITY.
   Whenever the free passage of any street or sidewalk in the city shall be
obstructed by a crowd, congregation, parade, meeting, assembly or procession,
or the conduct of two or more persons, except as authorized by any permit
issued pursuant to this chapter, the persons comprising such group shall
disperse or move when directed to do so by a police officer. It shall be
unlawful for any person to refuse, and such refusal shall be a violation of
this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-110) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 94.11 ENFORCEMENT.
   Nothing contained in this chapter shall prohibit the authority of any
officer to arrest a person engaged in any act or activity granted a permit
under this chapter, if the conduct of such person violates the laws of the
state, provisions of this code or ordinances of this city, or unreasonably
obstructs the public streets and sidewalks of this city, or engages in acts
that cause or would tend to cause a breach of the peace.
(Prior Code, § 14-111)
§ 94.12 OUTDOOR CONCERTS REGULATED.
   (A)   Any outdoor concert consisting of live or recorded music held in a
public park or other public area shall end by 9:30 p.m. and shall be conducted
in such a manner as to not disturb the peace of the city.
   (B)   This section shall not apply to community designated events.
(Prior Code, § 14-112) (Ord. 746, passed 10-4-1993; Ord. 1134, passed 4-4-2011)
Penalty, see §
10.99

   Cemeteries generally, see SDCL Ch. 34-27
GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 95.01 SCOPE.
   The cemetery owned and operated by the city and known as Rose Hill Cemetery
shall be governed, managed and operated under the provisions of this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-156) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   CEMETERY PARCEL. A grave space or another type of space to place human
remains in the cemetery.
   CEMETERY PARCEL DEED. A written instrument that conveys the right to place
human remains in the cemetery parcel so noted on the deed.
   CERTIFICATE OF PURCHASE FOR PERPETUAL CARE. A certificate granting the
purchaser of perpetual care the right to perpetual care of a cemetery parcel
purchased and perpetual care of the cemetery where the cemetery parcel is
located in accordance with SDCL Ch. 9-32 as in existence at the time of the
perpetual care purchase or as thereafter amended.
   CREMATION SPACE. A space intended to hold a maximum of two cremated remains
per space. A full-size burial may not be interred in a cremation space.
   DOUBLE BURIAL. A cemetery parcel in which two cremations or one cremation
and one full-size burial are placed.
   INDIGENT BURIAL. A burial paid for by the county for the benefit of a
qualified individual in need of financial assistance for a burial.
   INFANT SPACE. A cemetery parcel intended to hold one infant burial or one
infant cremated remains.
   LOT. The space in the ground of the cemetery that is made up of multiple
cemetery parcels. Cemetery parcels in a LOT may be owned by the same person or
different persons. The LOT is essentially a numbered, surveyed location.
   MONUMENT. A marker of varying shape and size cut from granite, marble,
bronze or rock and mortar which is placed on a cemetery parcel to memorialize
those interred at that location.
   PARKS DIVISION MANAGER. The manager of the parks division as created in this
code.
   RIGHTSHOLDER. The original purchaser or an assignee of the right to place
human remains in the cemetery in a designated cemetery parcel so noted on a
cemetery parcel deed.
   STACK BURIAL. A single cemetery parcel in which two full-size burials are
placed one on top of the other.
   VAULT. A container made of concrete, metal or equally hard material placed
in the ground designed to accept the casket or urn, primarily to keep the
ground from sinking over time.
(Prior Code, § 14-157) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.03 ADMINISTRATION AND OPERATION, GENERALLY.
   (A)   General supervision and care. The Director of Parks and Recreation
shall have general supervision and care of the cemetery and shall take care
that all cemetery parcels and cemetery property therein are kept in proper
order and condition. He or she shall take care that all cemetery parcels
endowed as provided for in this chapter are put and kept in such good order and
condition as their endowment contemplates. It is the duty of the Director of
Parks and Recreation to employ such personnel necessary to oversee the digging
of graves, to properly care for all trees, shrubbery, plants and grass growing
in the cemetery, to keep the driveways, walkways and fences in good condition
and to ensure compliance with the rules and regulations of the cemetery.
(Prior Code, § 14-158)
   (B)   Records generally.
      (1)   The finance office shall keep all records of the cemetery and shall
procure suitable books, forms or other records, written and electronic, for the
purpose of record keeping.
      (2)   The City Administrator shall designate an employee to sell the
cemetery parcels and sign the permit for disposition of dead human remains.
(Prior Code, § 14-159)
   (C)   Rules and regulations. The administration and operation of the
cemetery shall be under the Parks and Recreation Department. The Director of
Parks and Recreation may make rules and regulations regarding the
administration and operation of the cemetery, which will be kept on file in the
finance office.
(Prior Code, § 14-160)
(Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.04 HANDLING OF FUNDS.
   All money received from the sale of cemetery parcels, digging of graves,
perpetual care and other services about the cemetery shall be paid directly to
the city. Payments for perpetual care shall be used for the care and
maintenance of the cemetery in accordance with state law.
(Prior Code, § 14-161) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.05 RULES OF THE CEMETERY.
   The following rules apply to the cemetery.
   (A)   Unless placed prior to the adoption of this section, all markers shall
be placed on the west side of the space facing east. Foot stones shall be flush
with the surface of the ground.
   (B)   Fences, hedges or other obstructions around or on grave units or
around lots or cemetery parcels are prohibited.
(Prior Code, § 14-162) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 799, passed 4-15-1996;
Ord. 860, passed 4-19-1999; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.06 PLANTINGS OF TREES, SHRUBS, FLOWERS OR PLANTS.
   (A)   Except for those plantings provided by the city, the planting of
trees, shrubs, flowers or plants is prohibited, including on cemetery parcels
and in the Rose Garden.
   (B)   As existing plantings located on graves or in alleyways die or
obstruct maintenance operations, they will be removed and will not be replaced.
(Prior Code, § 14-163) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.07 CONCRETE BORDERS.
   Concrete borders around graves are not allowed. Corner markers may be placed
at the rightsholder’s expense. Corner markers shall be flush with the ground
and no larger than four square inches in surface area. If existing concrete
borders become unsightly or damaged, the city will remove the concrete border
and replace the area with grass.
(Prior Code, § 14-165) (Ord. 860, passed 4-19-1999; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.08 PERMANENT VASES.
   Permanent vases on a cemetery parcel must only be incorporated onto and
attached to the monument.
(Prior Code, § 14-166) (Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.09 MONUMENTS.
   (A)   Removal of monuments prior to burial. A monument may be removed before
grave digging and then replaced once the grave has been prepared. The monument
removal and replacement will be at the rightsholder’s expense.
(Prior Code, § 14-167)
   (B)   Location of monuments. Only one upright monument is allowed per
cemetery parcel. Additional monuments and foot stones must be flush with the
ground. The location of monuments on all graves shall be determined by the
cemetery staff. A permanent monument must be placed within two years of burial.
(Prior Code, § 14-168)
   (C)   Monument permit.
      (1)   A permit is required before placement, repair, engraving or
replacement of monuments. The permit must be obtained through the finance
office.
      (2)   The following information must be provided at least two business
days prior to the placement of the monument:
         (a)   Name of deceased and name and contact information for contact
person;
         (b)   Block, section, lot and space ID of which monument placement or
work is to be done;
         (c)   Name of the monument company doing the placement or work;
         (d)   Type of work to be done and date placement or work is to be
completed; and
         (e)   A diagram of the cemetery parcel showing exact placement of the
monument(s).
(Prior Code, § 14-169)
(Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1295, passed 11-19-2018; Ord. 1327, passed 9-
21-2020)
§ 95.10 INTERFERING WITH FUNERAL.
   Persons who have not accompanied a funeral to the cemetery shall not
congregate around a grave or vehicles while ceremonies are in progress.
(Prior Code, § 14-170) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 95.11 RECREATIONAL ACTIVITIES NOT PERMITTED.
   Recreational activities that impede or disrupt the quiet enjoyment of the
cemetery are not permitted.
(Prior Code, § 14-171) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 95.12 DISINTERMENT.
   Disinterment is allowed only upon receipt of a disinterment permit from a
funeral home.
(Prior Code, § 14-172) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
CEMETERY PARCELS
§ 95.25 PAYMENT FOR CEMETERY PARCEL AND PERPETUAL CARE.
   (A)   The Common Council shall determine, by resolution, all cemetery fees
including the prices for which the cemetery parcels are to be sold. Upon
payment in full for a cemetery parcel and perpetual care, the purchaser will
receive a cemetery parcel deed and certificate of purchase for perpetual care
executed by the Mayor and attested by the Finance Officer under the seal of the
city.
   (B)   No burials may be made upon a cemetery parcel for which the city has
not received full payment. Upon receipt of full payment, a cemetery parcel deed
will be issued. If there is an interment on a cemetery parcel for which full
payment has not been made, the city reserves the right to disinter the remains
and remove the burial, together with any monument or other structure thereon,
to some other portion of the cemetery equal in price to the amount paid on such
space, after the actual cost of removal has been deducted.
(Prior Code, § 14-182) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.26 USE OF CEMETERY PARCELS; RESALE PROHIBITED.
   (A)   All cemetery parcels shall be used for burial of human dead only and
may not be resold. Any attempted resale of a cemetery parcel without the
consent of the Director of Parks and Recreation is void and will result in the
cemetery parcel reverting back to the city.
   (B)   If a cemetery parcel is no longer needed by the rightsholder, the city
will purchase the cemetery parcel back from the rightsholder at the price the
rightsholder paid for it.
(Prior Code, § 14-183) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.27 ROSE GARDEN; PURCHASE OF SPACES; CARE OF ASHES; NAMEPLATES.
   (A)   Purchase of spaces at the Rose Garden. The burial or spreading of
ashes in the Rose Garden requires the purchase of a site for such burial or
spreading. Burial or spreading of ashes in the Rose Garden is only allowed in
designated areas, as determined by the Director of Parks and Recreation.
(Prior Code, § 14-184)
   (B)   Care of ashes. When the ashes of a cremated body are to be interred in
the cemetery or Rose Garden, the ashes must be in a durable urn or container
intended for burial of cremated remains made of wood, metal, glass, ceramic or
concrete. When burying cremated remains in the Rose Garden, the dimensions of
the container shall be no larger than one foot by one foot by one foot.
(Prior Code, § 14-185)
   (C)   Nameplates in Rose Garden. The only markers allowed in the Rose Garden
are five-inch by eight-inch nameplates, which shall have the deceased’s name,
date of birth and date of death printed on them. The nameplates must be
purchased through the cemetery office.
(Prior Code, § 14-186)
(Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1295, passed 11-
19-2018; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.28 CEMETERY PARCEL REGULATIONS.
   (A)   (1)   All interments in cemetery parcels shall be designated by the
rightsholder.
      (2)   If the rightsholder is deceased, an heir, beneficiary, personal
representative, executor or administrator of the estate of the deceased
rightsholder may designate any interments.
   (B)   The city will not give joint cemetery parcel deeds and certificates of
purchase. If persons hold cemetery parcels in partnership, by agreement among
themselves, the city will not undertake to enforce the agreements.
   (C)   When a rightsholder dies intestate, the heirs will be recognized
according to the laws of the state that are in force at the time of the death.
   (D)   Upon the death of the rightsholder, it shall be the duty of the heir,
heirs, beneficiary, beneficiaries, personal representative of the estate of
rightsholder, executor of the estate of rightsholder or administrator of the
estate of rightsholder to file full proof of cemetery parcel ownership within
the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-187) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.29 ITEMS PLACED ON GRAVES.
   Items placed on cemetery parcels are subject to the following restrictions.
   (A)   Wreaths, artificial flowers, shepherd’s hooks and devices similar to
shepherd’s hooks are allowed on cemetery parcels from October 1 through April 1
only.
   (B)   Except for the holidays listed in division (D) below, cone vases with
fresh cut flowers are the only items that can be placed on cemetery parcels
from April 1 through October 1.
   (C)   Items will be allowed on cemetery parcels three days prior to the
observed Memorial Day holiday and ten days following the observed Memorial Day
holiday.
   (D)   Items are allowed on cemetery parcels the Thursday before until the
Monday following the following holidays:
      (1)   Easter;
      (2)   Mother’s Day; and
      (3)   Father’s Day.
   (E)   Items may be placed on monuments and bases if they do not protrude
past the monument base. Items that are located on monuments or bases will be
removed if they protrude past the monument base.
   (F)   All flags and other decorations, funeral designs, cut flowers and all
other items placed on cemetery parcels will be removed by the city when they
become unsightly, damaged, impede maintenance operations or are not placed in
compliance with this section.
   (G)   All items that are subject to time limits under this section must be
removed at the expiration of those time limits. If the items are not removed,
they will be discarded.
   (H)   No glass containers or glass items of any type are permitted in the
cemetery. All glass containers or glass items located in the cemetery will be
removed.
   (I)   In no case are city employees responsible for items left on any
cemetery parcel. The city reserves the right to remove any item from the
cemetery.
   (J)   Benches and other structures are not allowed on cemetery parcels at
any time.
   (K)   Except for during the approved holidays listed above, decorations are
not allowed on cemetery parcels that have a flush marker.
(Prior Code, § 14-188) (Ord. 613, passed 4-6-1987; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1295, passed 11-19-2018; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
INTERMENT
§ 95.40 BURIAL APPLICATIONS.
   (A)   No burial in Rose Hill Cemetery or the Rose Garden will be allowed
until a burial application is completed.
   (B)   The following information is required:
      (1)   Name and address of applicant;
      (2)   Applicant’s relationship to the deceased;
      (3)   Name, date of birth and date of death of the person to be buried;
      (4)   Block, section, lot and space number in which burial is to be made;
      (5)   Name of the mortician in charge of the body; and
      (6)   Date and time of graveside service.
(Prior Code, § 14-206) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.41 ISSUANCE OF BURIAL PERMIT; PROCEDURES.
   After receiving the burial application, the city will stake and inspect the
cemetery parcel. Double burials and stack burials will be allowed if prior
arrangements have been made with the city. Temporary grave markers must be used
by all mortuaries. The city is not responsible for any temporary markers and
any temporary marker may be removed at the city’s discretion. Under normal
circumstances, the city is not responsible for digging the graves.
(Prior Code, § 14-207) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 700, passed 4-15-1991;
Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.42 VAULT REQUIRED.
   Any casketed burial placed in a cemetery parcel, except an infant space,
shall be placed in a vault. No wood or fiberglass vaults are allowed.
(Prior Code, § 14-208) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.43 INADVERTENT BURIAL OR DAMAGE.
   Any person who purchases any cemetery parcel shall, by such purchase, be
deemed to have agreed, on behalf of himself or herself and his or her heirs and
assigns, to hold the city harmless for any damages resulting from an
inadvertent burial in the wrong cemetery parcel or for any damage to any
monument, stone, marker, memorial or other improvement placed on the cemetery
parcel.
(Prior Code, § 14-209) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.44 VAULT COVERS.
   (A)   Vault covers are not allowed on graves. Existing vault covers must be
converted to a flush marker once the vault cover becomes damaged or otherwise
falls into disrepair.
   (B)   The determination of when a vault cover needs to be converted to a
flush marker will be at the city’s sole discretion. Costs associated with
converting the vault cover to a flush marker will be the responsibility of the
rightsholder or his or her heir, beneficiary, personal representative, executor
or administrator.
(Prior Code, § 14-210) (Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.45 INFANT SPACE.
   A container interred in an infant space shall not be larger than two feet by
three feet.
(Prior Code, § 14-211) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.46 DOUBLE BURIALS AND STACK BURIALS.
   (A)   No double burial or stack burial will be allowed in the cemetery
except as follows.
      (1)   Two people who were spouses at the time of the first person’s death
may have a double burial within a cemetery parcel if the second decedent is
cremated.
      (2)   This section does not pertain to the cremation sections.
   (B)   No more than two burials in a cemetery parcel shall be allowed.
   (C)   In a situation of a double burial involving a full burial and a
cremation, the full burial must be interred either at the same time the
cremation is interred or before the cremation is interred. If the cremation is
interred prior to the full burial, a disinterment permit is required before the
interment of the full burial may occur.
   (D)   In a situation of a stack burial, the city must be made aware of the
stack burial at the time of the initial burial so the initial burial is placed
at the proper depth.
(Prior Code, § 14-212) (Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
PERPETUAL CARE
§ 95.60 PERPETUAL CARE FUND CREATED.
   The Common Council shall create and maintain a permanent fund from the gifts
or bequests made by any person by will or otherwise, from all sums derived from
the sale of perpetual care and from sums that may be from time to time added
thereto by the Common Council and shall use such funds for the care and
maintenance of the cemetery.
(Prior Code, § 14-231) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.61 INVESTMENT OF FUND.
   The Perpetual Care Fund shall be invested with interest in such amounts as
may be determined by the Finance Officer and upon security as acceptable
according to state law.
(Prior Code, § 14-232) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.62 RECORDS AND ACCOUNTS OF FINANCE OFFICER.
   The City Finance Officer shall keep a permanent record of all moneys
received for the Perpetual Care Fund, and the amounts paid in or set aside for
general improvement and shall keep an accurate account of the interest received
and collected and how expended.
(Prior Code, § 14-233) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-
2020)
§ 95.63 AUDIT.
   The books and accounts of the Finance Officer and the securities on which
the Perpetual Care Fund is loaned shall be audited as required for all accounts
of the city by the State Department of Legislative Audit.
(Prior Code, § 14-234) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
§ 95.64 EXTENT OF CARE.
   Perpetual care may include the care and maintenance of grounds,
infrastructure and roads and the enlargement of the cemetery. Perpetual care
does not include the maintenance, upkeep or repair of any damage to any
memorial, other improvement or item placed on or in the cemetery parcel
purchased.
(Prior Code, § 14-235) (Ord. 599, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 927, passed 8-5-2002;
Ord. 1327, passed 9-21-2020)
CHAPTER 96: PARKS AND RECREATION
Section
