GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 152.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   MANUFACTURED HOME.
      (1)   A moveable or portable unit, designed and constructed to be towed
on its own chassis (comprised of frame and wheels, whether or not such wheels
have been removed) and designed to be connected to utilities for year-round
occupancy. The term shall include:
         (a)   Units containing parts that may be folded, collapsed or
telescoped when being towed and that may be expanded to provide additional
cubic capacity;
         (b)   Units composed of two or more separately towable components
designed to be joined into one integral unit capable of being separated again
into the components for repeated towing.
      (2)   The term MANUFACTURED HOME shall include units designed or
designated to be used for residential, commercial, educational or industrial
purposes, excluding, however, recreational vehicles and other trailers and also
excluding manufactured homes, recreational vehicles and other trailers placed
on the grounds of the Black Hills Airport pursuant to a ground lease. For
purposes of this chapter and Appendix A to Ord. 1201, the terms manufactured
home and mobile home shall be interchangeable.
   MANUFACTURED HOME PARK OR SUBDIVISION. Any parcel (or contiguous parcels) of
land divided or arranged into two or more manufactured home lots for owner
occupancy, rent or sale.
   MANUFACTURED HOME SPACE. A defined plot of ground or lot within a
manufactured home park which is designed for and designated as the location for
two or more automobiles and one manufactured home, and not used for any other
purposes whatsoever other than the customary accessory uses.
(Prior Code, § 12-1) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014; Ord. 1279, passed 5-7-2018)
§ 152.02 NONCONFORMING USE.
   Any manufactured home within the city limits and not in a manufactured home
park or campground is hereby declared a nonconforming use.
(Prior Code, § 12-2) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
MANUFACTURED HOME PARKS AND SUBDIVISIONS
§ 152.15 MINIMUM STANDARDS.
   (A)   All manufactured home parks/subdivisions shall comply with the
requirements of §
156.060.
   (B)   The owner of a manufactured home park shall at all times operate the
park in compliance with the revised ordinances of the city and shall provide
adequate supervision to maintain the park, its facilities and equipment in good
repair in a clean and sanitary condition at all times.
(Prior Code, § 12-3) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.16 MAINTENANCE.
   The owner of a manufactured home park shall at all times operate the park in
compliance with the revised ordinances of the city and shall provide adequate
supervision to maintain the park, its facilities and equipment in good repair
and in a clean and sanitary condition at all times.
(Prior Code, § 12-4) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.17 OWNER’S RIGHT OF ENTRY TO MAKE REPAIRS.
   It shall be the duty of every occupant of a manufactured home park to give
the owner thereof or his or her agent or employee access to any part of such
manufactured home park or its premises at reasonable times for the purposes of
making such repairs or alterations as are necessary to effect compliance with
this subchapter, or with any lawful regulations adopted thereunder or with any
lawful order issued pursuant to the provisions of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 12-5) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
PLACEMENT AND CONNECTION PERMIT
§ 152.30 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to set up, place, establish or connect
to utilities any manufactured home within the jurisdiction of the city without
first obtaining a placement and connection permit issued by the City Building
Official. The permit fee shall be as established by resolution as approved by
the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 12-6) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 152.31 PLACEMENT OF MANUFACTURED HOMES.
   The placement of a manufactured home located on any lot within the
jurisdiction of the city shall meet the requirements of this chapter and must
be located according to the requirements of §
156.060(A). If the owner of the manufactured home also owns the lot where the
home is placed, the home shall be placed on a foundation approved by the
Building Official. Manufactured homes located within a manufactured home park
or leased lot may either be placed on a permanent foundation or on footing pads
and piers as approved by the Building Official.
(Prior Code, § 12-7) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.32 CONDITIONS OF SUPPORT AND ANCHORING.
   All manufactured homes shall be supported and anchored in accordance with
the manufacturer’s installation instructions, the federal model manufactured
home installation standards (24 C.F.R. part 3285) or as approved by the
Building Official.
(Prior Code, § 12-8) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.33 INITIAL INSPECTION.
   All blocking, piers, anchoring, plumbing and mechanical work shall be
completed and inspected by the Building Official prior to the installation of
skirting. Only the area directly behind a landing or deck may be skirted prior
to the required inspection. Manufactured homes may not be occupied until the
initial inspection has been completed and approved.
(Prior Code, § 12-9) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.34 FINAL INSPECTION.
   A final inspection of the manufactured home by the Building Official is
required upon the installation of skirting, porches, steps, landings and
guardrails. Approved residential numbering must be attached to the home prior
to final inspection:
      (A)   The location and width of roadways and walkways;
      (B)   The location of water and sewer lines, storm drains and catch
basins; and
      (C)   The location and size of the recreation area.
(Prior Code, § 12-10) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.35 DRAINAGE.
   Every manufactured home park shall be located on a well-drained site and
shall be so located that its drainage will not endanger any water supply.
Individual manufactured homes shall be placed to provide positive drainage
around the home.
(Prior Code, § 12-11) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014)
§ 152.36 USE OF SPACES GENERALLY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person operating a manufactured home park to
allow any manufactured home to be occupied unless the manufactured home is
situated on a manufactured home space.
(Prior Code, § 12-12) (Ord. 1201, passed 10-20-2014) Penalty, see §
10.99

   Sidewalks, see SDCL §§ 9-46-1 et seq.

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 153.001 BUILDING PERMIT.
   A building permit shall be required with the requisite fees associated
therewith prior to the construction of sidewalks and driveways required by the
city.
(Prior Code, § 14-1) (Ord. 518, passed 11-10-1982)
§ 153.002 STREET GRADES.
   The grades of the streets and avenues in the city as theretofore established
and as shown on the street profiles on file in the office of the Public Works
Administrator are hereby adopted as the official record of the street grades in
the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-26)
Statutory reference:
   Authority to establish street grades, see SDCL §§ 9-45-1 and 9-45-14
§ 153.003 STREET NAME, PREFIXES; OFFICIAL MAP.
   (A)   The names of the streets lying easterly from Main Street shall be
designated as “East” and the names of the streets lying westerly of Main Street
shall be designated as “West.” The prefixes shall be placed before the proper
names of the street as “East Colorado Street” or “West Colorado Street.”
   (B)   The names of the streets and avenues in the city are hereby fixed and
adopted in accordance with and as shown by the map of the city on file in the
office of the Public Works Administrator, which map is hereby designated and
adopted as the official map of the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-27)
Statutory reference:
   Name of streets, avenues, see SDCL § 9-45-2
§ 153.004 OBSTRUCTION OF GUTTERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place, cause or maintain any
obstruction of whatsoever manner in any gutter or drainage ditch within the
city.
(Prior Code, § 14-28) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.005 REMOVAL, REPLACEMENT OF CURBS AND GUTTERS.
   (A)   No person shall remove or cause to be removed any portion of existing
curb and gutter without first obtaining a written permit to do so from the
Public Works Administrator. No such permit shall be issued for removal of curb
and gutter except in accordance with the provisions contained herein.
   (B)   Application for such permit must be made in writing upon forms
furnished by the city. Such application shall contain the name and address of
the person making the application and the name and address of the contractor or
person who is to replace the curb and gutter.
   (C)   All such work shall be done under the jurisdiction of the Public Works
Administrator and in accordance with this code and shall be inspected upon
completion by the constituted member of such department.
   (D)   All plans and specifications must conform to the following minimum
requirements before a permit for removal and replacement shall be issued.
      (1)   The replacement of curb and gutter must conform to the existing
curb and gutter grade as established and designated by the official grades of
the streets of the city and the profile on file in the office of the Public
Works Administrator.
      (2)   If an existing expansion joint in the curb and gutter is within
five feet of the end of the driveway opening, the existing curb and gutter may
be removed to the expansion joint, otherwise the existing curb and gutter must
be cut, making a neat edge truly at right angles to the edge of the pavement
and truly vertical.
      (3)   The new curb and gutter shall be constructed in a manner and of a
material equal at least to the existing curb and gutter adjacent thereto.
   (E)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of the property
owner who removes or causes any other person to remove any portion of curb and
gutter to provide the costs for all materials, construction and installation
involved in replacing the curb and gutter, and all construction and
installation shall be performed according to plans and specifications of the
city.
(Prior Code, § 14-29)
§ 153.006 DRIVEWAYS.
   (A)   For the purpose of this section, PARKWAY means the portion of the
public right-of-way which lies between the curb and gutter and the adjacent
property line or, if no curb and gutter is present, it is the portion of the
public right-of-way which lies between the edge of the paved street and the
adjacent property line.
   (B)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of all property
owners whose driveway connects to an existing paved street, paved alley or
crosses over a public parkway to install a nonporous concrete or bituminous
driveway surface. The following are exceptions to this requirement.
      (1)   In locations where the existing street or alleyway providing access
to the property is unpaved, the driveway shall be surfaced with asphalt,
concrete, gravel, asphalt millings or similar loose material.
      (2)   For property zoned Rural Large Lot Single-Family or Agricultural, a
paved surface is only required when the existing street providing access to the
property is paved, in which case the paving of the driveway shall be required
to extend only to the front setback and with a minimum width of 12 feet. Beyond
the front setback, gravel, asphalt millings or similar loose material is
permitted.
   (C)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of all property
owners whose driveway crosses over any portion of any public sidewalk or public
parkway to provide the costs for all materials, construction and installation
involved in surfacing the driveway with nonporous concrete or bituminous
material.
   (D)   Where a driveway of any kind of material is constructed across the
public sidewalk or public parkway, it shall conform to the sidewalk grades as
established and designated by the official grades of the sidewalks of the city
and the profiles on file in the office of the Public Works Administrator.
   (E)   All driveways shall be so graded between the gutter and the sidewalk
that it will not be necessary to change the established grade of either and
will not elevate or depress any portion of either. No part of such driveway
shall extend beyond the curbline in such manner as to change the grade of such
gutter or obstruct the free flow of water in such gutter. Where elevations or
depressions are necessary in the parkway strip adjoining the curb and walks,
the parkway shall be graded on both sides of the driveway to a distance
sufficient to create a gradual ascent or descent. Where driveways cross open
ditches in the parkways, adequate culverts shall be installed.
(Prior Code, § 14-30) (Ord. 1165, passed 11-19-2012; Ord. 1231, passed 1-19-
2016)
§ 153.007 SURFACING OF AREAS AS BEHIND LAY-DOWN CURBS.
   (A)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of the property
owner whose property adjoins or abuts lay-down curbing to install within six
months a nonporous concrete or bituminous surface upon the area behind the lay-
down curbing which is used for parking, loading, unloading or delivery
purposes.
   (B)   It shall be the responsibility hereafter and required of such property
owner to provide the costs for all materials, construction and installation
involved in laying the nonporous concrete or bituminous surface.
(Prior Code, § 14-31)
§ 153.008 MOVING OF BUILDINGS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to move a building of any kind
over the streets or alleys of this city without first paying a fee of $50 and
obtaining a permit to do so from the Public Works Department.
   (B)   When a permit shall be granted for the purpose of moving a building
over the streets of the city, it shall be the duty of the Public Works
Department to verify that the moving person or company has been licensed by the
city and submitted a certified check in the amount of $1,000 to cover any
damages to the city property which might result from such use of the streets
and alleys under the operation of such permit.
   (C)   When the building has been moved as contemplated and allowed by a
permit under this section, it shall be the duty of the Public Works
Administrator to carefully examine the route over which such building was
moved. If the person to whom such permit was granted repairs forthwith any
damages to the full satisfaction of the Public Works Administrator, the
certified check collected as herein provided shall be refunded. Otherwise the
Public Works Administrator shall cause such damages to be repaired and pay for
the same out of the certified check so collected and held by him or her and
refund the remainder, if there be any, to the person from whom collected.
(Prior Code, § 14-32) (Ord. 844, passed 6-1-1998) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.009 LOCATION OF STREET LIGHTS.
   (A)   Residential street lights within the city may be placed at
intersections. If there is a distance of over 400 feet between intersections or
on a dead-end street over 400 feet with a cul-de-sac, the Public Works
Department shall determine the need and best location for a light and make such
recommendation to the Public Works Committee.
   (B)   The locations or spacing of street lights in commercial or major
thoroughfares shall be determined by the Public Works Department. Such location
shall be based upon recommendation of the applicable electric company as to
candle power and coverage of light and shall be the most efficient and
economical to the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-33) (Ord. 601, passed 9-15-1986)
§ 153.010 RIDING ON TOY VEHICLES PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person traveling upon any coaster, sled, roller
skates or any toy vehicle to ride upon any street in the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-34) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.011 SNOW REMOVAL.
   (A)   Policy. It is hereby declared to be in the public interest to regulate
and restrict the parking and operation of vehicles on public streets during
snow removal efforts.
(Prior Code, § 14-36)
   (B)   Snow storm information and advisory guide. The City Administrator is
hereby required to establish and maintain an administrative policy entitled the
City Snow Information and Advisory Guide which describes how the city will
address snow removal and regulate such things as parking in snow conditions.
The policy has the weight of law.
(Prior Code, § 14-37)
   (C)   Interference or obstruction of snow removal operations. It shall be
unlawful for any person or operator of any vehicle to interfere with or
obstruct, or cause interference with or obstruction, of the snow removal
operations undertaken by the city and its employees. It shall also be unlawful
for any person to operate any vehicle in a manner not reasonable or prudent,
thereby creating a safety risk in relation to snow removal operations.
(Prior Code, § 14-38)
   (D)   Placement of snow. Residents and businesses shall not be allowed to
place snow on public boulevards and public streets. Exception: Property owners
in the Downtown Business Improvement District who have no ability to store snow
on site will be allowed to push snow onto the street if done before the city
plows or removes snow. Any snow placed on the right-of-way along with snow
already on the street cannot exceed three feet in height.
(Prior Code, § 14-39)
   (E)   Responsibility for snow removal on private driveways. The city will
not plow snow from private property and will not open any private driveways
whether closed by city street plowing or other means. Property owners will be
responsible for snow removal of sidewalks in compliance of this section.
(Prior Code, § 14-40)
   (F)   Additional power of administrative staff. The administrative staff
shall have the power, during extreme snow removal circumstances, to close any
street or portion of street which is under the jurisdiction of the city to all
traffic and parking, if necessary, for public safety and efficient removal of
snow.
(Prior Code, § 14-41)
(Ord. 817, passed 2-18-1997; Ord. 1112, passed 11-2-2009) Penalty, see §
153.999
OBSTRUCTIONS AND ENCROACHMENTS
§ 153.025 DEFINITION.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definition shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ENCROACHMENT. Any sign, awning, canopy or marquee, billboard or other
advertising device, merchandise stand or display, building or other structure
or other use for private purposes of any character which exists in or rests
upon or projects above the right-of-way or any portion thereof of a public
street.
(Prior Code, § 14-51) (Ord. 1342, passed 4-5-2021)
§ 153.026 RESTRICTED.
   It shall be unlawful, except as hereinafter provided, for any person to
erect, construct, install, place, maintain or allow to remain or to permit the
erection, construction, installation, placing, maintenance or remaining of any
encroachment upon or above the right-of-way or any portion thereof, in the city
unless permitted by an encroachment agreement with the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-52) (Ord. 1342, passed 4-5-2021) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.027 NONCONFORMING ENCROACHMENTS.
   Any encroachment existing on the effective date of the ordinance from which
this subchapter was derived, as heretofore permitted by the city, may be
continued for a period of 90 days from and after such effective date unless
discontinued, or unless the same shall become defective and unsafe prior to the
expiration of such period, in which case the same shall be removed by the owner
or person permitting the erection, construction, installation, placing or
maintenance of the same; provided, however, that in established business
districts on such streets where the buildings are at the property line and are
continuous or very closely spaced, overhanging encroachments are permitted
under the following conditions.
      (A)   Awnings, canopies, marquees and similar installations supported
wholly from the face of the building shall be permitted, providing that the
edge of such encroachment be not less than three feet back of the face of the
curb.
      (B)   Advertising or other similar signs supported wholly from the front
of the building shall be permitted to remain in place until such time that they
become functionally or structurally obsolete; such signs shall then be removed.
      (C)   The replacements of encroachments, as allowed in division (B)
above, will not be permitted.
(Prior Code, § 14-53)
§ 153.028 OBSTRUCTION OF TRAFFIC DEVICES.
   In the event the encroachments referred to in §
153.027 by reason of color or placement, obscure or in any way detract from the
effectiveness of highway signs or traffic signals, the city may cause the
removal of such encroachments in the manner hereinafter provided for the
removal of any encroachment in violation of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-54)
§ 153.029 USE OF RIGHT-OF-WAY.
   The use of the right-of-way by owners or lessees of abutting property for
the storage of vehicles, placement of portable signs or other private use,
without an encroachment agreement, is hereby prohibited on public rights-of-
way.
(Prior Code, § 14-55) (Ord. 1342, passed 4-5-2021) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.030 DISPLAY OF GOODS PROHIBITED.
   The use of sidewalks or other areas of the right-of-way for the storage or
display of merchandise without an encroachment agreement, is prohibited on
public rights-of-way.
(Prior Code, § 14-56) (Ord. 1342, passed 4-5-2021) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.031 REMOVAL.
   Whenever any encroachment exists in violation of the provisions of this
subchapter, the city will issue notice requiring the removal of such
encroachment within a specified time. If the owner or person responsible for
such encroachment, or his or her agent, is known, such notice will be a written
notice served in person or by certified mail upon such owner or agent. If the
owner, person responsible or agent is unknown, notice will be posted on or near
the encroachment or on the adjacent property. If the owner, person responsible,
agent or the adjacent property owner fail or refuse to remove the encroachment
within the time fixed in the notice, the city shall cause the encroachment to
be removed. Upon removal of the encroachment, all related receipts and
administrative costs will be billed to the owner, person responsible, agent or
adjacent property owner.
(Prior Code, § 14-57) (Ord. 1342, passed 4-5-2021)
§ 153.032 PERMISSION FOR ARTWORK.
   Any person desiring to place sculpture, statuary, fountains or other artwork
of any kind on or over public property shall first obtain permission from the
Common Council, which shall approve the artwork and location thereof. Such
artwork may not constitute a safety or traffic hazard.
(Prior Code, § 14-60) (Ord. 901, passed 9-17-2001)
§ 153.033 CERTAIN CHURCH SIGNS PERMITTED.
   Notwithstanding any ordinance or zoning regulation to the contrary, each
church located within the city shall be allowed to use the public right-of-way
to place two directional and informational signs not exceeding 720 square
inches per sign on each side. Both sides of a sign may be used if the sign is
hung by a bracket. No fee or permit is required for such sign.
(Prior Code, § 14-61) (Ord. 958, passed 6-16-2003)
SIDEWALKS
§ 153.045 INSTALLATION.
   (A)   Unless exempt under Ch. 154 or Ch. 156, it shall be the responsibility
hereafter and required of all property owners of vacant lots, that sidewalks be
installed whenever a new building or dwelling be constructed upon such vacant
lots.
   (B)   Such sidewalks shall be completed at or before the time the new
building or dwelling is completed and shall be constructed and installed
according to city plans and specifications on file in the office of the Public
Works Administrator.
(Prior Code, § 14-76) (Ord. 922, passed 4-1-2002)
§ 153.046 LOCATION OF SIDEWALKS.
   (A)   Sidewalks constructed in the city shall be located in conformity with
existing sidewalk locations, except the replacement of sidewalks abutting the
curb, whenever possible, shall conform to the standards of this section.
   (B)   In the event no existing sidewalk location and in the case of new
subdivisions, sidewalk location shall be as follows:
      (1)   Five feet from and parallel to the back of the curb; and
      (2)   If no curb exists, parallel to and adjacent to the lot line.
   (C)   The Common Council may permit exceptions where special conditions
warrant.
(Prior Code, § 14-77) (Ord. 697, passed 3-4-1991)
§ 153.047 SPECIFICATIONS.
   All sidewalks within this city shall be constructed and maintained in
compliance with specifications therefor promulgated in the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-78)
§ 153.048 DISCHARGE OF RAINWATER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to permit the rainwater from any
building discharge on and over the sidewalks.
(Prior Code, § 14-79) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.049 SIDEWALK SNOW AND ICE CONTROL.
   Property owners are responsible for controlling snow and ice buildup on
sidewalks.
(Prior Code, § 14-81)
§ 153.050 BUILDING PERMITS REQUIRED PRIOR TO BUILDING OF SIDEWALKS AND
DRIVEWAYS.
   (A)   A building permit shall be required with the requisite fees associated
therewith prior to the construction of sidewalks and driveways required by the
city.
   (B)   Section 301(b)(7) of the Uniform Building Code adopted in §
150.015 adopted by the city is repealed and all other provisions of such Code
inconsistent with this section are likewise repealed.
   (C)   Unless changed by ordinance of the city, the provision exempting
sidewalks and driveways in any future edition of the Uniform Building Code
which may hereafter be adopted by the city will likewise be repealed and
ineffective.
(Prior Code, § 14-82)
§ 153.051 RESTRICTIONS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to erect, construct, install, place or
to permit the erection, construction, installation, placing of any encroachment
upon or above any portion of any residential sidewalk in the city.
(Prior Code, § 14-83) (Ord. 703, passed 6-3-1991) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.052 REMOVAL.
   Whenever any encroachment exists in violation of these provisions, written
notice shall be given to the owner of record requiring removal within 14 days.
If the owner of record fails to remove the encroachment within the time
specified in the notice, the city shall remove the encroachment at the owner’s
expense.
(Prior Code, § 14-84) (Ord. 703, passed 6-3-1991)
§ 153.053 PUBLIC SIDEWALK MAINTENANCE.
   The maintenance of sidewalks located in city right-of-way including, but not
limited to, the area between the property line and street curb shall be the
responsibility of the owner, manager or lessee of the abutting property. Such
persons are jointly and severally liable for the maintenance and replacement
when required by the city according to the criteria pertaining to sidewalk
replacement.
(Prior Code, § 14-85) (Ord. 1165, passed 11-19-2012)
USE OF CITY RIGHTS-OF-WAY AND OTHER PROPERTIES
§ 153.065 SUPERVISION.
   The City Engineer or his or her designee shall supervise all excavations
made for any purpose in the streets, alleys or public ground and shall require
compliance with all the requirements of this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 14-131) (Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)
§ 153.066 PERMIT REQUIRED.
   (A)   No person shall make or cause to be made any excavation in or under
any street, parking, sidewalk, alley or public ground without first having
obtained a ROW permit and a contractor’s license from the Building and
Development Department. The permit will not be required to start emergency work
as may be necessary to protect existing structures. However, the permit shall
be obtained the morning of the first working day after such work has commenced.
   (B)   Any person, other than a person holding a special event permit,
desiring to block, partially occupy or interrupt the traffic flow of any ROW
for 30 minutes or more for any reason, shall be required to have a ROW permit.
   (C)   The construction of driveways and sidewalks within the city’s
corporate limits pursuant to a city building permit will include a ROW permit
at no extra charge.
   (D)   Any person starting any work in a municipal ROW without a ROW permit
shall be subject to fines set forth in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 14-132) (Ord. 880, passed 4-17-2000; Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-
2015)
§ 153.067 APPLICATION FOR PERMIT.
   (A)   Any person requesting a ROW permit shall make application to the City
Engineer or his or her designee.
   (B)   At a minimum, the application shall include the exact location of the
excavation, a detailed description of the work to be performed, the purpose for
the excavation, an illustration of the areas to be disturbed or removed and a
timeline for the replacement of all materials. The City Engineer may approve
temporary repairs in the event of inclement weather.
   (C)   Additional submittal documents, such as traffic control plans and
utility plans or profiles, may be required as determined by the City Engineer,
based on the size or complexity of the project or other factors.
   (D)   Only licensed contractors may perform curb or street repairs.
(Prior Code, § 14-133) (Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)
§ 153.068 PERMIT FEE.
   The fee for a ROW permit shall be the minimum base charge set by resolution,
per excavation, up to and including 400 feet. Beyond 400 feet, the permit fee
will be charged by the foot, commensurate with the base charge listed above. A
service repair permit shall be obtained in lieu of a ROW permit for repair of
water or sewer service lines. The permit fee for the repair of city water and
sewer service lines shall be waived.
(Prior Code, § 14-134) (Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)
§ 153.069 CONDITION OF ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Every application for a ROW permit that involves excavation in or
under any street, parking area or sidewalk shall be accompanied by:
      (1)   A certificate of insurance showing that the applicant has in effect
a statutory workers’ compensation insurance policy in the amount of limits
applicable for the state;
      (2)   A certificate of insurance showing that the applicant has
occurrence-based commercial general liability insurance or equivalent form,
with a limit of not less than $1,000,000 for each occurrence. If such insurance
contains a general aggregate limit, it shall apply separately to this ROW
permit or be no less than two times the occurrence limit. Such insurance shall
add the city and its employees as additional insureds. Such certificate shall
contain a statement to the effect that the policy cannot be canceled or
substantially altered without ten days prior written notice to the city; and
      (3)   A certificate of insurance showing that the applicant has
automobile liability insurance, with a limit of not less than $1,000,000 for
each accident. Such insurance shall include coverage for owned, hired and non-
owned vehicles. Such certificate shall contain a statement to the effect that
the policy cannot be canceled or substantially altered without ten days’ prior
written notice to the city.
   (B)   Each ROW permit issued shall contain a statement and shall be issued
only upon the express condition that the permittee shall refill the excavation
in accordance with the instructions of the City Engineer and restore the
pavement or surfacing, as the case may be, to its former condition and maintain
it in such condition for a period of three years from the time of completion of
the work authorized by the ROW permit.
(Prior Code, § 14-135) (Ord. 780, passed 8-21-1995; Ord. 880, passed 4-17-2000;
Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)
§ 153.070 REFILLING EXCAVATIONS.
   The City Engineer shall adopt, amend and enforce a code of rules and
regulations which shall set forth the manner in which various types of
excavations shall be replaced.
(Prior Code, § 14-136) (Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)
§ 153.071 RESTORING PAVEMENTS OR STREET SURFACING TO MEET CITY SPECIFICATIONS.
   It shall be the duty of the City Engineer to keep on file a copy of all ROW
permits, and to conduct periodic inspections of pavements or other street
surfacing disturbed pursuant to such permits. If a pavement or surface is not
restored to current city specifications, notice thereof shall be sent to the
permittee. The permittee shall return the pavement or surface to an approved
condition within a time period as specified by the City Engineer. If the
permittee fails to restore and maintain such pavement or the surfacing thereof,
the City Engineer shall arrange for the completion of the necessary repairs.
The original permittee shall pay a penalty to the city equal to one and one-
half times the cost of the repairs. No other permit shall be issued to an
individual, or any person on his or her behalf, until satisfaction of the
penalty provided by this section has occurred. The City Engineer shall be
consulted for typical street patching requirements.
(Prior Code, § 14-137) (Ord. 1044, passed 1-2-2007; Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-
2015)
§ 153.072 PROTECTION OF PUBLIC AND SURROUNDING PROPERTIES.
   (A)   Any person receiving a permit to make excavations in or upon any
street, alley, sidewalk or public ground shall, during the progress and
continuance of the work, erect and maintain around the project area, both by
day and night, suitable guards, fences, lanterns and signals so as to prevent
injury to persons, animals or vehicles on account of such excavations. Such
lanterns shall be kept lighted from sundown until sunrise. Traffic control will
be determined by the City Engineer, based on the specific project and its
proximity to roadways. If a traffic control plan is required, the contractor
will be required to use State Department of Transportation (SDDOT) standard
traffic control plates, which will be filed with the ROW permit application.
Larger projects may require traffic control plans implemented by a SDDOT-
approved contractor.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person, owner or occupant of any lot to
make or cause to be made any excavation adjacent to any street, alley, public
ground, sidewalk or traveled road or roadway, unless appropriate measures are
implemented to prevent the injury of any person or animal.
   (C)   Any person making an excavation shall use all appropriate control
measures to prevent pollutants from entering neighboring properties and waters
of the state, including municipal storm drain conveyances and natural drainage
ways.
(Prior Code, § 14-138) (Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015) Penalty, see §
153.999
§ 153.073 DITCH COMPACTION.
   The city will not allow water soaking for compaction of trenches resulting
from utility placement or repairs. All trenches will be mechanically tamped and
compacted to a compaction factor of 95% or greater. Testing of the trench
compaction may be required, at the discretion of the City Engineer.
(Prior Code, § 14-140) (Ord. 602, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 1044, passed 1-2-2007;
Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)
§ 153.074 SIDEWALK SERVICE PERMIT.
   (A)   The Public Works Director may permit a food or beverage service
establishment (establishment) to sell and allow to be consumed food or
beverages on a sidewalk or walkway subject to a public right-of-way abutting
and immediately adjacent to the food or beverage service establishment’s
premises.
   (B)   The establishment must submit a sidewalk service permit application
with the following.
      (1)   The establishment shall propose a specific service area that
clearly delineates the boundaries where food or beverages may be served and
consumed. The service area cannot impede pedestrian use of the sidewalk and
must provide a minimum width of 60 inches of clear space for pedestrian use.
The service area shall meet existing requirements of the building code.
      (2)   The establishment shall propose a seating configuration that
maintains ADA accessible walkways and employs commercial grade tables, chairs,
umbrellas, benches or other furniture, the design and construction of which
shall be subject to approval of the Public Works Director.
      (3)   The establishment shall propose a plan to address any garbage and
waste that may be generated by the proposed use.
   (C)   The establishment may install a physical barrier or other visual
delineation to designate the service area. If the establishment chooses to
install a physical barrier, the design and materials must be approved by the
Public Works Director prior to construction. The barrier must follow all
relevant building regulations.
   (D)   The establishment must have a valid sidewalk service permit and
provide a copy of the establishment’s certificate of insurance that lists the
city as an additional insured. The establishment must agree to any and all
conditions or restrictions the city may deem appropriate based on the location
or other characteristics of the establishment.
   (E)   The city may revoke the sidewalk service permit at its discretion or
if the establishment violates any of the provisions of this section or other
laws or regulations.
(Prior Code, § 14-141) (Ord. 1331, passed 10-5-2020)
§ 153.999 PENALTY.
   (A)   Any person violating any provision of this chapter for which no
specific penalty is prescribed shall be subject to §
10.99.
   (B)   In the event any person fails to comply with the provisions of §
153.005, he or she shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and fined not less than
$50.
(Prior Code, § 14-29)
   (C)   In the event any person fails to comply with the provisions of §
153.006, he or she shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and fined not less than
$50.
(Prior Code, § 14-30)
   (D)   In the event any person fails to comply with the provisions of §
153.007, he or she shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-31)
   (E)   Violation of any provisions of §
153.011, in addition to the penalties contained herein, may be punished by a
fine in accordance to a Class 2 misdemeanor. Illegally parked vehicles may be
ticketed, towed and impounded at owner’s expense. Enforcement of any provisions
of §
153.011 will be in compliance of §§
70.20 through
70.30.
(Prior Code, § 14-42)
   (F)   Any person violating §§
153.065 through
153.074 shall be subject to fines set forth in §
10.99.
(Prior Code, § 14-140)
(Ord. 602, passed 9-15-1986; Ord. 817, passed 2-18-1997; Ord. 1044, passed 1-2-
2007; Ord. 1221, passed 12-21-2015)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 154.001 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ADMINISTRATIVE OFFICIAL. The officer appointed by the city to administer
this chapter.
   BOND. A security consisting of a cash deposit, surety bond, personal
guarantee, collateral, property or instrument of credit in an amount and form
satisfactory to and approved by the Common Council whenever a bond is required
by this chapter.
   CITY ENGINEER. The person designated by the Common Council to furnish
engineering assistance for the administration of this chapter.
   CUL-DE-SAC. A local street with only one outlet and having an appropriate
turn-around at its terminus for the safe and convenient reversal of traffic
movement.
   DEDICATION. The designation and formal transfer of land to the governing
body for use by the public.
   EASEMENT. A grant of the right to use land for specific purposes.
   FINAL PLAT. The map, plan or record of subdivision and any accompanying
material, as described in this chapter.
   LOT. A tract, plot or portion of subdivision or other parcel of land
intended as a unit for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of transfer of
ownership or of building development.
   LOT LINE REVISION. The re-subdivision of an existing platted lot for the
purpose of adjusting boundary lines.
   LOW DENSITY. Subdivisions having an average density of one and one-half lots
per acre or less.
   MAJOR STREET PLAN. The map showing the streets and highways laid out,
adopted or established by law, any amendments or additions thereto resulting
from the approval of subdivision plats and the subsequent filing of such
approved plats.
   MAJOR SUBDIVISION. All subdivisions of four or more lots.
   MINOR SUBDIVISION. Any subdivision containing not more than three lots.
   PRELIMINARY PLAT. The map, plan or record of proposed subdivision and any
accompanying material approved by the Common Council in advance of the
submission of a final plat.
   SKETCH PLAN. The preliminary drawing or drawings, referenced in this
chapter, indicating the proposed manner and layout of the subdivision to be
submitted for approval.
   STREET, COLLECTOR. A road intended to move traffic from residential streets
to minor arterials.
   STREET, MAJOR ARTERIAL. A road of considerable continuity, which is
primarily a through-traffic artery for interconnection among large areas.
   STREET, MINOR ARTERIAL. A road supplementary to the major streets and
primarily a means of interconnection between minor traffic-generating areas.
These streets carry traffic from collector streets to the major arterial
streets.
   STREET, RESIDENTIAL. A lane, minor, major or low-density residential street
intended to provide access to other roads from abutting properties.
   SUBDIVISION. Any land, vacant or improved, which is divided or proposed to
be divided into two or more lots, parcels, sites, units, plots or interests for
the purpose of offer, sale, lease or development, including re-subdivision.
SUBDIVISION includes the division of land, whether by deed, metes and bounds
description, devise, intestacy, lease, map, plat or other recorded instrument.
   TIME. Days for public notice and shall include the day of notice but not the
day of hearing and shall include weekends and holidays.
(Prior Code, § 15A-1) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.002 PURPOSE.
   The regulations in this chapter are adopted to establish reasonable
standards of design and procedures for subdivisions, to protect and provide for
the public health, safety and general welfare of the city, to promote
aesthetically attractive subdivisions and to achieve economies in the
construction and long-term maintenance of the city street system.
(Prior Code, § 15A-2) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.003 CONFLICTING REGULATIONS.
   Where any provision of this chapter imposes restrictions different from
those imposed by any other provision of this chapter, or any other ordinance,
rule or regulation, or other provision of law, whichever provisions are more
restrictive or impose higher standards shall control. These regulations are not
intended to abrogate any easement, covenant or any other private agreement or
restriction.
(Prior Code, § 15A-3) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.004 JURISDICTION.
   This chapter shall govern all subdivisions of land within the corporate
boundaries of the city.
(Prior Code, § 15A-4) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.005 FEES.
   The application fee for preliminary and final plat approval shall be
according to the Planning and Zoning Department fee schedule adopted by
resolution of the City Council.
(Prior Code, § 15A-5) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1159, passed 7-16-2012)
§ 154.006 PREPARATION.
   All plats shall be prepared and sealed by a registered land surveyor
licensed to practice in the state.
(Prior Code, § 15A-6) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
PROCEDURE
§ 154.020 GENERALLY.
   The applicant or a designated agent shall attend each meeting where action
is requested. If represented by an agent, such designation shall be in writing
and filed with the application.
(Prior Code, § 15A-21) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.021 ADMINISTRATIVE APPROVAL OF PLATS.
   Pursuant to the authority granted in SDCL § 11-3-6, the administrative
official of the city may approve final plats in lieu of approval by the
governing body subject to the following regulations.
   (A)   Minor subdivisions (three lots or less) may be approved by the
administrative official.
   (B)   Major subdivisions (four lots and more) may be approved by the
administrative official under the following circumstances:
      (1)   A preliminary plat of the subdivision has been approved by the
Common Council and the final plat is in conformance with the same;
      (2)   A planned unit development has been approved by the Common Council
and the final plat is in conformance with the same; and
      (3)   Lot line revisions or subdivision of existing lots result in a
major subdivision, so long as the subdivision conforms to the density
requirements of the applicable zoning district.
(Prior Code, § 15A-22) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1377, passed 3-6-2023)
§ 154.022 GOVERNING BODY APPROVAL OF PLATS.
   (A)   The following is required for minor subdivisions plat approval:
      (1)   Application, fee and, for all properties where changes in the
floodplain are proposed, written verification from FEMA that the letter of map
change has been approved;
      (2)   Sketch plan approval by administrative official;
      (3)   Prepare final plat and submit Mylar, one full-size copy (to scale),
one 11 by 17 copy and electronic format compatible with the city system. The
electronic format requirement may be waived for any firm that does not have
electronic drafting equipment;
      (4)   Public hearing by Planning Commission, with five days’ notice;
      (5)   Recommendation to the Common Council;
      (6)   Approval or disapproval by the Common Council; and
      (7)   Recording.
   (B)   The following is required for major subdivisions plat approval:
      (1)   Application, fee and, for all properties where changes in the
floodplain are proposed, written verification from FEMA that the letter of map
change has been approved;
      (2)   Sketch plan approval by administrative official;
      (3)   Prepare preliminary plat and submit seven copies;
      (4)   Public hearing by the Planning Commission, with five days’ notice;
      (5)   Recommendation to the Common Council;
      (6)   Approval or disapproval by the Common Council;
      (7)   Prepare final plat and submit Mylar, one full-size copy (to scale),
one 11 by 17 copy and electronic format compatible with the city system. The
electronic format requirement may be waived for any firm that does not have
electronic drafting equipment;
      (8)   If no substantial changes, plat shall be forwarded by the
administrative official to the Planning Commission Chair and Mayor for
signatures, subject to requirements for bond, dedication and form; and
      (9)   Recording.
(Prior Code, § 15A-23) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1009, passed 7-5-2005;
Ord. 1053, passed 3-5-2007)
§ 154.023 INFRASTRUCTURE COMPLETION PRIOR TO RECORDING FINAL PLAT.
   (A)   No final plat may be recorded for any lot within a subdivision before
the installation, dedication and acceptance of all public improvements
including, but not limited to: paved streets; curb; gutter; sidewalk; water
lines; sewer lines; and drainage improvements. The City Council may grant a
special exception to allow a delay in the completion of any improvements by
agreement secured by a letter of credit, bond, cash escrow deposit or other
guarantee of such improvements.
   (B)   Exceptions for plats recorded before July 5, 2005: Where no street
improvements exist but a final plat is recorded, these provisions shall not
prohibit the city from issuing a building permit; provided, that the permit is
issued with notice to the contractor/owner that no garbage collection or
plowing of the street can take place until final street improvements are
installed.
(Prior Code, § 15A-24) (Ord. 1009, passed 7-5-2005; Ord. 1222, passed 12-21-
2015)
DOCUMENT REQUIREMENTS
§ 154.035 PRELIMINARY PLAT.
   (A)   Vicinity map, street names.
      (1)   A vicinity map or key map shall accompany or be shown on the
preliminary plan or sketch plan at a legible scale showing all existing
subdivision streets, tract lines or acreage parcels adjoining the proposed
subdivision. It shall show how streets in the proposed subdivision connect with
existing and proposed streets in adjoining subdivisions and future street
openings to undeveloped property to produce the most advantageous development
of the adjoining area.
      (2)   The subdivider shall submit proposed street names for E-911
approval with the preliminary plat or sketch plan.
   (B)   Minor subdivision. A sketch plan may be submitted as a preliminary
plat for a minor subdivision. If the property proposed for development involves
areas where it would be desirable to impose additional requirements, the
administrative official may require some or all the data contained in the
requirements for preliminary plat, major subdivisions.
   (C)   Major subdivision. The plat submitted shall be of such scale that all
survey, mathematical information and all other details are clearly and legibly
shown. Each lot and block shall be lettered or numbered. The area in square
feet and dimensions of all boundaries of each lot shall be shown. The plat
shall also show:
      (1)   The proposed name of the subdivision;
      (2)   North arrow, scale;
      (3)   Proposed legal description;
      (4)   The boundary line (accurate in scale) of the tract to be
subdivided;
      (5)   Topographic map with minimum five-foot contours;
      (6)   Drainage plan and, if applicable, a FEMA floodplain map overlay;
      (7)   The names of adjacent property owners and lot descriptions;
      (8)   The location, widths and names of all existing or platted streets
or other public ways within or adjacent to the tract;
      (9)   All parcels of land intended to be dedicated for public use or
reserved in the deeds for use of all property owners in the proposed
subdivision, together with the purpose of conditions or limitations of such
reservation, if any;
      (10)   The layout, names (if previously approved) and widths of existing
and pro-posed streets and easements;
      (11)   When required by the Planning Commission, the preliminary plat
shall be accompanied by:
         (a)   The profile of each street with tentative grades for a
reasonable distance beyond the limits of the subdivision; and
         (b)   The cross-section of proposed streets showing the width of
roadways, locations and width of sidewalks. All elevations shall be based upon
mean sea level datum.
      (12)   Where a replat of an existing plat is being submitted for
consideration, the location of the existing plat shall be indicated by
insertion of broken lines and a statement, where appropriate, vacating the
former plat.
   (D)   Floodplain revisions. At the time of preliminary plat submittal, the
applicant shall provide a copy of the letter of map change request as submitted
to the Flood Emergency Management Agency (FEMA). If there is no floodplain on
the subject property, this requirement may be waived if not applicable. The
city may refuse to accept a preliminary plat without this letter and may also
refuse to accept a preliminary plat where a floodplain may exist and the
Floodplain Administrator has made a written determination that a letter of map
change is required. All floodplain revisions shall comply with §
151.47.
(Prior Code, § 15A-41) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1009, passed 7-5-2005)
§ 154.036 FINAL PLAT.
   (A)   The final plat shall be submitted in the form of one Mylar, one full-
size copy (to scale), one 11 by 17 copy and electronic format compatible with
the city system. The electronic format requirement may be waived for any firm
that does not have electronic drafting equipment.
   (B)   The final plat shall be drawn to scale of not more than one inch
equals 100 feet and shall show:
      (1)   The name and legal description of subdivision;
      (2)   The name and address of the owner;
      (3)   North arrow, scale;
      (4)   The boundary lines with accurate distances and bearings, the exact
location and widths of all existing or recorded streets and ways intersecting
the boundary of the tract;
      (5)   True bearings and distances to the nearest established street lines
or official monuments, which shall be accurately described on the plat;
municipal, township, county or section lines accurately tied to the lines of
the subdivision by distances and bearings;
      (6)   An accurate vicinity map of the subdivision in reference to the
real estate records of the county including names of adjacent recorded owners
of property;
      (7)   Streets and alleys together with approved names;
      (8)   The length of all arcs, radii, internal angles and points of
curvature;
      (9)   All existing and proposed easements and rights-of-way provided for
public services, utilities or access and any limitations of the easements;
      (10)   All block indications, lot numbers and lot lines with accurate
dimensions in feet and hundredths, and bearings or angles in degrees, minutes
and seconds;
      (11)   The accurate location, material and approximate size of all
monuments;
      (12)   The designation of easements and rights-of-way and all property
which is offered for dedication for the public use, with the purpose indicated
thereon, and of all property that may be reserved by deed covenant for the
common use of the property owners in the subdivision; and
      (13)   Monuments shall be located and/or set at each angle and curve
point on the outside boundary lines of the plat, at all block corners and at
all intermediate points on the block lines indicating a change of direction in
the lines. The plat shall indicate that the monuments have been set or found.
(Prior Code, § 15A-42) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1053, passed 3-5-2007)
VARIANCES
§ 154.050 HARDSHIP.
   (A)   An applicant who is able to show an extraordinary hardship arising
from the location, topography or other physical characteristic, which would
make it difficult or impossible to conform strictly to this chapter, may apply
for a variance.
   (B)   The Common Council, upon finding that such conditions do exist and
that the public interest shall be secured and that such project will be
beneficial to the community and not nullify the intent and purposes of the
comprehensive plan or this chapter, may vary the regulations so that
substantial justice may be done.
(Prior Code, § 15A-61) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.051 CONDITIONS.
   In granting variances and modifications, the Common Council may require such
conditions as will secure substantially the objectives of the standards or
requirements so varied or modified.
(Prior Code, § 15A-62) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.052 PROCEDURE.
   Application for a variance shall be made concurrently with the submission of
the preliminary plat.
(Prior Code, § 15A-63) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
DESIGN STANDARDS
§ 154.065 MINIMUM STANDARDS.
   The following requirements of design and development are to be considered as
minimum standards.
(Prior Code, § 15A-81) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.066 DUTIES OF SUBDIVIDER.
   (A)   All of the following improvements are to be constructed by the
subdivider.
   (B)   A statement by the Public Works Department that the following
requirements have been met and approved shall accompany the final plat:
      (1)   Typical sections and profiles of the proposed streets showing
widths and grades of roadways, types of surfacing, curb locations and width and
location of sidewalks;
      (2)   Preliminary layout plan and profiles of proposed sanitary and storm
sewers, with tentative grades, pipe sizes and the location of appurtenances;
      (3)   Preliminary layout plan and profiles of the proposed water
distribution system showing tentative pipe sizes and location of appurtenances;
and
      (4)   Lighting plan.
(Prior Code, § 15A-82) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.067 RELATION TO ADJOINING STREET SYSTEM.
   (A)   A subdivision shall provide for the continuation of the principal
streets existing in the adjoining subdivisions or of their proper projection
when adjoining property is not subdivided, and such streets shall be of a width
not less than the minimum requirements for streets set forth in the regulations
of this chapter.
   (B)   Where the plat submitted covers only a part of the subdivider’s tract,
drawing of the prospective future street system of the entire tract shall be
furnished and the street system of the part submitted shall be considered in
light of conformity to the street system of the entire tract.
   (C)   Where a tract is subdivided into lots of an acre or more, the Planning
Commission may require an arrangement of lots and streets such as to permit a
later subdivision in conformity to the street requirements and other
requirements contained in this chapter.
(Prior Code, § 15A-83) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.068 ACCESS.
   The subdividing of the land shall be such as to provide each lot, by means
of public street or way, with satisfactory access to an existing public street
or to a thoroughfare as shown in the major street plan, or an official map.
(Prior Code, § 15A-84) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.069 STREET WIDTHS.
   In order to provide for roads of suitable location, width and improvement to
accommodate prospective traffic and afford satisfactory access to emergency
services, snow removal, sanitation and road maintenance equipment and to
coordinate roads so as to compose a convenient system and avoid undue hardships
to adjoining properties, the following minimum design standards for roads are
hereby required.

NOTES:
1.   Residential traveled street width is based on moving lanes of ten feet,
parking lanes of nine feet.
2.   Traveled width does not include gutter, when required. Gutter width is
included in width of parking lanes.
3.   Where required, sidewalk width shall be five feet, setback five feet
from curb or edge of pavement. Wheelchair ramps shall be provided at all
intersections.
4.   ADT (average daily traffic) is based on ten trips per single-family
residential dwelling unit, per day.
5.   All streets shall be improved with a wearing surface approved by the
city.
6.   Curb/gutter is not required only when a drainage plan for surface water
discharge has been approved by the Public Works Administrator.
 
(Prior Code, § 15A-85) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1165, passed 11-19-
2012)
§ 154.070 STREET GRADES AND CONDITION.
   (A)   The grades of streets shall not exceed 10%, except under unavoidable
conditions approved by the Planning Commission at the time of preliminary plat
approval.
   (B)   All streets shall have at least a 0.3% grade.
   (C)   All streets shall be improved with a wearing surface approved by the
city.
(Prior Code, § 15A-86) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.071 STREET CURVES.
   Minimum centerlines of curvature, tangents, curb radiuses and sight
distances shall be based on design speed as per the Institute of Transportation
Engineers, Traffic Engineering Handbook, current edition.
(Prior Code, § 15A-87) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.072 ALLEYS.
   Alley rights-of-way, if provided, shall not be less than 20 feet in width.
The corners of all alley intersections with other alleys or streets shall have
a radius of not less than ten feet.
(Prior Code, § 15A-88) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.073 HALF STREETS.
   No half streets shall be included in a subdivision plan except where
necessary on the boundary of the subdivision tract where the extension of an
existing dedicated street must be provided for and the boundary line of the
tract is the centerline of the necessary street.
(Prior Code, § 15A-89) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.074 EASEMENTS.
   (A)   Accessible and unobstructed utility easements of not less than five
feet in width shall be provided on each side of the rear and side lot lines.
   (B)   Easements of the same or greater width may be required along lot lines
or across lots or land parcels when required by the administrative official.
(Prior Code, § 15A-90) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.075 BLOCKS.
   (A)   No blocks shall be longer than 1,200 feet between street lines. In
blocks over 800 feet in length, there shall be a cross walkway easement of not
less than ten feet in width, near the middle of the block.
   (B)   The width of blocks shall be such as to allow two tiers of lots,
unless exceptional conditions are, in the opinion of the Planning Commission,
such as to render this requirement undesirable.
(Prior Code, § 15A-91) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.076 LOTS.
   Every lot shall abut on a street improved to the standards required by this
chapter. The minimum dimensions of residential lots on any plat shall be in
conformity with the zoning ordinance.
(Prior Code, § 15A-92) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.077 CURB AND GUTTER.
   Concrete curb and gutter shall be provided as required in §
154.069 and may be required on all residential streets to accommodate drainage.
(Prior Code, § 15A-93) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.078 RIGHT-OF-WAY WIDTH.
   Widths of rights-of-way shall be as required by §
154.069.
(Prior Code, § 15A-94) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.079 WATER AND SEWER FACILITIES.
   (A)   The subdivider is required to connect to the municipal water and
sewerage systems and must install all facilities according to the
specifications of the Public Works Department. Service lines must be stubbed to
every lot abutting a street prior to the surfacing of the street.
   (B)   For lots eight acres and larger zoned Rural Large Lot Single-Family
(RLS-1) and located at a distance greater than otherwise required by state law
or city code to be connected to a sanitary sewer, connection to the municipal
water and sewer system is not required. Private/shared wells and private
disposal systems are permitted and must be designed and stamped by a registered
professional engineer.
   (C)   Except where otherwise prohibited by law, easement, ordinance or other
more restrictive regulation, for lots one acre and larger zoned Agriculture
(AG) and located at a distance greater than otherwise required by state law or
city code to be connected to a sanitary sewer, connection to the municipal
sewer system is not required. Private disposal systems are permitted and must
be designed and stamped by a registered professional engineer. Connection to
the municipal water system is required.
   (D)   Wires for locating water and sewer services must be installed
(attached to outside of line) with new or replacement lines from the main to
the outside of the structure it serves. (This will not be required on existing
lines until the line is replaced.)
   (E)   Stubbed water lines will include curb stop, curb box and rod extension
from curb valve to top of the curb box.
   (F)   Water and sewer services stubbed into properties must be marked at top
of curb with a “W” and an “S” respectively.
(Prior Code, § 15A-95) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002; Ord. 1045, passed 4-2-2007;
Ord. 1165, passed 11-19-2012; Ord. 1334, passed 10-19-2020)
§ 154.080 UTILITIES.
   All utilities shall be located underground throughout the subdivision unless
the Planning Commission waives this requirement because of hardship. If there
are existing utility facilities aboveground, such facilities may qualify for
hardship treatment. Underground service connections to every platted lot shall
be installed.
(Prior Code, § 15A-96) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
§ 154.081 DRAINAGE FACILITIES.
   (A)   A subdivision which does not make provision for storm or floodwater
runoff, during and after construction, may not be approved. Rights-of-way may
be required where it is deemed necessary to provide adequate drainage, to
accommodate upstream drainage, to minimize the effects of downstream drainage,
and to adequately interface with the existing stormwater drainage system of the
city. Drainage plans shall be in compliance with the master drainage plan,
where applicable.
   (B)   The property owner ultimately assumes all responsibility for drainage
off individual lots.
(Prior Code, § 15A-97) (Ord. 914, passed 2-19-2002)
CHAPTER 155: TREES AND LANDSCAPING
Section

TREES
§ 155.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this subchapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BOARD. The Urban Forestry Board created by §
155.02.
   FORESTER. The person employed by the city who has direct responsibility for
implementing and enforcing this subchapter.
   PARK TREES. The trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation on
public lands.
   PEST. Any organism, insect, rodent or other agent that damages or causes
abnormal growth, disease or death of any tree, shrub, bush or woody vegetation.
   STREET TREES. Trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation on lands
lying within municipal rights-of-way.
(Prior Code, § 19-26) (Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 607, passed 1-19-1987;
Ord. 651, passed 3-20-1989)
§ 155.02 URBAN FORESTRY BOARD.
   (A)   Established, composition, appointment. There is hereby established an
Urban Forestry Board which shall consist of seven residents of the city,
appointed by the Mayor with the approval of the Common Council. The county
agent and City Public Works Administrator shall serve as ex-officio members of
the Board.
(Prior Code, § 19-51)
   (B)   Terms, compensation, organization.
      (1)   The terms of office of the Board members shall be three years.
Members appointed to the Board shall be appointed in staggered terms. In the
event a vacancy shall occur during the term of any member, a successor shall be
appointed for the unexpired portion of that term.
      (2)   Members of the Board shall serve without compensation.
      (3)   The Board shall choose its own officers and shall keep a journal of
the proceedings. Three members shall constitute a quorum.
(Prior Code, § 19-52)
   (C)   Duties. The duties of the Urban Forestry Board are as follows:
      (1)   The Board shall develop a city tree plan.
      (2)   The Board, when requested by the Common Council, shall consider,
investigate, make findings, reports and recommendations upon any special matter
or question coming within the scope of its work.
(Prior Code, § 19-53)
   (D)   Review by Council. Any decision of the Board may be appealed to the
Common Council within seven days of such decision.
(Prior Code, § 19-54)
(Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 607, passed 1-19-1987; Ord. 645, passed 11-
21-1988; Ord. 704, passed 6-3-1991)
§ 155.03 STREET AND PARK TREES.
   (A)   No street tree shall be planted unless the Urban Forestry Board shall
have first approved the kind, size, variety and location thereof and granted a
permit therefor. The permit shall be issued without charge.
   (B)   A list of trees and shrubbery suitable for street trees shall be
developed by the Board.
   (C)   Care of street trees shall be the responsibility of the owner of the
abutting property.
   (D)   (1)   It shall be unlawful for any person to top any street or park
tree.
      (2)   For the purpose of this section, TOPPING is defined as the cutting
back of limbs to stubs more than six inches in diameter or trimming within the
crown to such a degree as to remove the normal canopy and disfigure the tree.
      (3)   Trees severely damaged by storms or other causes, or interfering
with utility services or similar obstructions may be topped with the approval
of the Board.
   (E)   Stumps of street and park trees shall not project above the surface of
the ground.
   (F)   The city shall have the right to plant, prune, maintain and remove
trees, plants and shrubs within rights-of-way and on public grounds.
   (G)   The city may remove or cause to be removed, any tree or part thereof
which is infested with any pest or is in an unsafe condition or is injurious to
sewers, electric power lines, gas lines, water lines or other public
improvements or which interferes with public walkways, streets, highways or
alleys.
(Prior Code, § 19-71) (Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 607, passed 1-19-1987)
Penalty, see §
155.99
§ 155.04 DESTRUCTION OF STREET AND PARK TREES.
   When the city must destroy street trees to install or repair water and sewer
lines, the property owner may be awarded up to $15 per tree replacement
matching funds. The funds shall be paid to property owner upon receipt of proof
of purchase and planting. Private utility companies shall be responsible for
the same matching funds as specified herein when operating within city rights-
of-way.
(Prior Code, § 19-72) (Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 645, passed 11-21-1988)
§ 155.05 TREES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY.
   (A)   Dead, dying, diseased, decayed and defective trees or other woody
plants that create a public safety hazard or harbor pests and/or infections
harmful to other vegetation are hereby declared a public nuisance. Any tree
displaying signs of an Emerald Ash Borer presence, Dutch Elm Disease, Chestnut
Blight, Oak Wilt or any other wilt disease or invasive species presence are
hereby declared a public nuisance.
   (B)   The city shall have the right to inspect and remove or cause to be
removed, in full or in part, any tree or woody plant determined to be a
nuisance on private property. The city will notify the property owner, agent or
occupant that the tree is a public nuisance and direct the property owner,
agent or occupant to abate the nuisance. The notice and order to abate will be
in writing and sent by certified mail, return receipt requested or hand
delivery. In the event the owner fails to correct the nuisance within the
stated time frame, the city may abate the nuisance and charge the cost of
abatement and administrative costs to the property owner, agent or occupant. If
full payment is not received within 30 days, the city may tax the cost of the
abatement and administrative costs by special assessment against the real
property.
   (C)   City staff will prepare a nuisance tree determination form explaining
how a tree is noncompliant. A copy will be sent to the owner(s) with the
official notice.
   (D)   A person who is the subject of a nuisance notice and order to abate
may appeal the order to the Common Council by submitting a written appeal to
the City Council within seven days from the date the notice is postmarked or
hand delivered.
   (E)   If, in the city’s determination, a tree or woody plant poses an
immediate threat to human life or safety, the city may immediately remove the
threat.
(Prior Code, § 19-73) (Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 607, passed 1-19-1987;
Ord. 1343, passed 4-19-2021)
§ 155.06 STORAGE OF DEAD OR CUT TREES.
   No person shall store or permit the accumulation of any elm wood in the
city. No person shall store any tree or part thereof known to harbor or contain
any pest infestation or declared to contain any pest infestation.
(Prior Code, § 19-74) (Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 607, passed 1-19-1987)
Penalty, see §
155.99
§ 155.07 INTERFERENCE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to prevent, delay or interfere with the
city or any of its agents engaged in the planting, cultivation, mulching,
pruning, spraying, inspecting or removing of any trees within the city as
authorized by this subchapter.
(Prior Code, § 19-75) (Ord. 541, passed 5-16-1983; Ord. 607, passed 1-19-1987)
Penalty, see §
155.99
§ 155.08 CARE AND MAINTENANCE OF CITY RIGHT-OF-WAY.
   (A)   The care, mowing and maintenance of city rights-of-way, including, but
not limited to, the area between the property line and street curb shall be the
responsibility of the owner, manager or lessee of the abutting property.
   (B)   Such persons are jointly and severally liable for the care,
maintenance and mowing.
(Prior Code, § 19-76) (Ord. 830, passed 10-20-1997; Ord. 952, passed 4-21-2003)
§ 155.09 WILT DISEASE AND INVASIVE SPECIES.
   The city is hereby required to establish and maintain an administrative
policy entitled the city’s wilt disease and invasive species response plan
which describes how the city will address and regulate such things as storage
of wood and removal of trees during an outbreak of a disease or an invasive
species. The policy has the weight of law.
(Prior Code, § 19-77) (Ord. 1343, passed 4-19-2021)
§ 155.10 HAZARDOUS TREE EMERGENCY DECLARATION.
   When evidence confirms the presence of diseases or invasive species, such as
the Emerald Ash Borer, the Mayor and Council may declare a hazardous tree
emergency. During a hazardous tree emergency, the city’s wilt disease and
invasive species response plan will guide city policy on tree maintenance,
removal and storage of wood. An emergency event will end once the Mayor and
Council declare the emergency to be over.
(Prior Code, § 19-78) (Ord. 1343, passed 4-19-2021)
§ 155.11 ADDITIONAL POWER OF ADMINISTRATIVE STAFF.
   The administrative staff shall have the power, during a hazardous tree
emergency declaration, to close any park, street, sidewalk or portion of street
or sidewalk which is under the jurisdiction of the city to all public use, if
necessary, for public safety and efficient removal and maintenance of impacted
trees. City staff or agents may enter private property to remove any infected
wood or trees.
(Prior Code, § 19-79) (Ord. 1343, passed 4-19-2021)
LANDSCAPING
§ 155.25 PURPOSE.
   (A)   The purpose of this subchapter is to provide for the orderly, safe,
healthful and aesthetic development of the city and to promote the health,
safety and general welfare of the community.
   (B)   The objectives of this subchapter are as follows:
      (1)   To aid in regulating and controlling vehicular and pedestrian
circulation in parking areas;
      (2)   To enhance the environmental and aesthetic conditions of the
community;
      (3)   To protect and enhance the value of property and to provide
wildlife habitat; and
      (4)   To reduce heat and noise, wind and air turbulence and the glare of
sunlight and vehicle lights, erosion and air pollution.
(Prior Code, § 19-100) (Ord. 698, passed 3-18-1991)
§ 155.26 LANDSCAPING REQUIRED.
   Landscaping conforming to the standards set forth in this section shall be
required in the following districts:
   (A)   Multiple-Family Residential District (R-3), excepting single-family
use;
   (B)   All commercial districts;
   (C)   All industrial districts; and
   (D)   Parking lots in any zoning district that are designed for 50 vehicles
and more.
(Prior Code, § 19-101) (Ord. 698, passed 3-18-1991)
§ 155.27 LANDSCAPE REQUIREMENTS.
   The following requirements are considered to be minimum and shall be
approved on the basis of a landscape plan submitted by the applicant to the
Building Official, accompanied, when required, by a guarantee approved by the
City Attorney, and installed as per the approved plan.
   (A)   The amount and type of material shall be based on a point system
determined by the square footage of a lot not covered by a building. In phased
development, the Planning Commission shall determine lot area for the purpose
of this subchapter. Trees, shrubs, grass and ground cover, both existing and
proposed, shall receive points towards landscape requirements according to the
following table:
LANDSCAPE MATERIAL POINTS TABLE
  New Landscape Material (Points) Existing Mature Landscape Material (Points)

                                        New Landscape     Existing Mature
                                        Material (Points) Landscape Material
                                                          (Points)
Grass             1 square yard         10                10
                  A minimum mature
                  spread of 45 feet.
Large trees       Conifers which reach  2,000             5,000
                  a mature height over
                  20 feet

                  spread of 25 feet.

                  mature height of at

                  in height

                  height of 2 feet
                  A minimum mature
                  spread of 15 feet.
